data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p><strong>Processing file:</strong> Orthopedics Complete Nursing Kmtc Notes.pdf</p></div></div></div><div class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="orthopedic-nursing">Orthopedic nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orthopedic-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>By Japheth mulwa</p>
<p>Objectives By the end of the unit the learner will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>To review A &amp;P of the bones</li>
<li>Describe bone injury healing process</li>
<li>To discuss fractures and the principles of fracture management.</li>
<li>To discuss indications and care of patients done amputation of a limb</li>
<li>To describe causes and management of orthopaedic diseases</li>
<li>Identify congenital malformations related to orthopaedics and discuss their management</li>
<li>Apply knowledge of orthopaedic management in nursing patients presenting with orthopaedic conditions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Anatomy and physiology of the bones</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Assessment to include:- Hx, physical exam, neurovascular assessment, and investigations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Minor injuries:- Contusion, Lacerations, Strains, Sprains &amp; dislocations/subluxation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fractures:- Definition, types/classification, clinical features, general principles of management</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amputation and its management(definition, indications, management)</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>orthopedic diseases (osteomyelitis;arthritis;osteoporosis &amp; osteomalacia</p>
<ul>
<li>Congenital abnormalities:- Talipes, Congenital hip dislocation &amp; osteogenesis imperfecta</li>
<li>Tumors i.e. benign and malignant</li>
<li>Gout and pagets’ disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="orthopedic-nursing">Orthopedic nursing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orthopedic-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Orthopedic nursing is a nursing specialty focused on the prevention and treatment of musculoskeletal disorders. This may range from acute problems such as fractures or hospitalization for joint replacement to chronic systemic disorders such as loss of bone density or lupus erythematosus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-of-the-anatomy-and-physiology-of-the-musculoskeletal-system">Review of the anatomy and physiology of the musculoskeletal system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-of-the-anatomy-and-physiology-of-the-musculoskeletal-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d092af9c.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<p>© Elsevier Ltd. Drake et al: Gray's Anatomy for Students <a href="http://www.studentconsult.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">www.studentconsult.com</a></p>
<ul>
<li>The science concerned with the study of bones is termed <strong>osteology</strong>.</li>
<li>The skeletal system of an adult is composed of approximately <strong>206 bones</strong>. Each bone is an organ of the skeletal system.</li>
<li>For the convenience of study, the skeleton is divided into <strong>axial</strong> and <strong>appendicular parts</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p>80 axial bones these includes the head, facial, hyoid, auditory, trunk, ribs and sternum</p>
<ul>
<li>126 appendicular bones. This includes arms, shoulders,wrists ,hands, legs, hips, ankles and feet</li>
</ul>
<p>Axial bones- the bones that line up along the central core of your body</p>
<p>Appendicular bones- bones that support the appendages</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Bone (oseous) is one of the hardest structures of the body. It possesses also a certain degree of toughness and elasticity. Its color, in a fresh state, is pinkish-white externally, and red within.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-bones">Types of bones<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-bones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-93cef0c8.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>There are 5 main types of bones</li>
<li>Long bones- characterized by a long shaft, like a femur</li>
<li>Short bones- roughly cubed shaped and found in wrist</li>
<li>Flat bones-are thin and curved bones with two hard bones sandwiching a soft tissue, the skull bones</li>
<li>Irregular bones- bones that do not fit in the above categories, like hip or spine bones</li>
<li>Sesamoid bones- bones that are embedded in tendons, like the patella</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definitions">definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The periosteum- a thin layer of connective tissue that covers the outer surface of a bone in all places except at joints</li>
<li>The endosteum- a thin vascular membrane of connective tissue that lines the inner surface of the bony tissue that forms the medullary cavity of long bones</li>
<li>The epiphyseal growth plate is the main site of longitudinal growth of the long bones</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-composition-of-the-bone">CHEMICAL COMPOSITION of the bone<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-composition-of-the-bone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Bone matter consists of two types of chemical material:</p>
<ul>
<li>Organic – 1/3, mainly collagen (it provides elasticity to the bone).</li>
<li>Inorganic – 2/3, mainly calcium phosphate (provides hardness to the bone).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-bone-cells">Types of bone cells<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-bone-cells" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Osteogenic cells respond to traumas, such as fractures, by giving rise to bone-forming cells and bone-destroying cells.</li>
<li>Osteoblasts (bone-forming cells) synthesize and secrete unmineralized ground substance and are found in areas of high metabolism within the bone.</li>
<li>Osteocytes are mature bone cells made from osteoblasts that have made bone tissue around themselves. These cells maintain healthy bone tissue by secreting enzymes and controlling the bone mineral content; they also control the calcium release from the bone tissue to the blood.</li>
<li>Osteoclasts are large cells that break down bone tissue. They are very important to bone growth, healing, and remodeling.</li>
<li>Bone-lining cells - made from osteoblasts along the surface of most bones in an adult. Bone-lining cells are thought to regulate the movement of calcium and phosphate into and out of the bone.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="continuation">continuation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#continuation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hematopoietic- found in the bone marrow, its function is to produce red blood cells, white blood cells and platelets</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="histology-of-bone-bone-tissues">Histology of bone. Bone tissues<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#histology-of-bone-bone-tissues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>On examining a cross section of any bone, it is composed of two kinds of bony tissue:</li>
<li>Compact tissue, it is dense in texture and it is always placed on the exterior of the bone.</li>
<li>Cancellous tissue/ spongy consists of slender fibers and lamellae, which join to form a reticular structure and it is placed in the interior of the bone</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-dd98c4fb.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg">
© Elsevier Ltd 2005. Standing: Gray's Anatomy 39e</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="function-of-bone">Function of bone<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#function-of-bone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Haemopoiesis</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The bone marrow consists of:</li>
<li>red bone marrow</li>
<li>yellow bone marrow</li>
<li>The white or yellow marrow fills up the medullary cavities of the shafts of the long bones.</li>
<li>The red marrow is located within the cancellous tissue and extends into the larger bony canals (Haversian canals) that contain blood vessels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="haemopoiesis-function">Haemopoiesis function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemopoiesis-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The bone marrow provides haemopoiesis function and biological protection of the organism. It takes part in nutrition, development and growth of the bone. The red marrow concerned with haemopoiesis and bone formation, has an active role in the healing of fractures. Red marrow predominates in infants and in children, with growth of child the red marrow is gradually replaced by yellow marrow.</p>
<p>NB: The bones of the embryo and new-born contain only red marrow.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="haemopoiesis-function">Haemopoiesis function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#haemopoiesis-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The red bone marrow of an adult produces white blood cells, red blood cells, and platelets.</li>
<li>In an infant, the spleen and liver produce red blood cells, but as the bones mature, the bone marrow performs this task.</li>
<li>It is estimated that an average of 1 million blood cells are produced every second by the bone marrow to replace those that are worn out and destroyed.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Mineral storage</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The inorganic matrix of bone is composed primarily of minerals calcium and phosphorus. These minerals give bone rigidity and account for approximately two-thirds of the weight of bone.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>About 95% of the calcium and 90% of the phosphorus, within the body, are stored in the bones and teeth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In addition to calcium and phosphorus, lesser amounts of magnesium and sodium salts are stored in bones.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-support-weight">3. Support (weight<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-support-weight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Lymph Vessels and Nodes of Head and Neck</p>
<p>SEE ALSO PLATE 204</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-24e86fac.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>The skeleton forms a rigid framework to which are attached the soft tissues and organs of the body.</li>
</ul>
<p>PLATE 68</p>
<p>HEAD AND NECK</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-protection-function">4. Protection function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-protection-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Protection is assured by the property of the bones to form body cavities which protects the vital important organs.</p>
<ul>
<li>The skull and vertebral column enclose the central nervous system.</li>
<li>The thoracic cage protects the heart, lungs, great vessels, liver and spleen.</li>
<li>The pelvic cavity supports and protects pelvic organs.</li>
<li>Even the site where blood cells are produced is protected within the central portion of certain ones.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-811f5f2c.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
© Elsevier Ltd. Drake et al: Gray's Anatomy for Students <a href="http://www.studentconsult.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">www.studentconsult.com</a></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-body-movement">5. Body movement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-body-movement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Bones serve as anchoring attachments for most skeletal muscles. In this capacity, the bones act as levers, with the joints functioning as pivots, when muscles, which are regulated by the nervous system, contract to cause the movement.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-66bbecf1.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-aab0515f.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg">
© Elsevier Ltd 2005. Standring: Gray's Anatomy 39e</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ossification-of-the-bones-bone-development">OSSIFICATION OF THE BONES/ BONE DEVELOPMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ossification-of-the-bones-bone-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Two types of ossification (osteogenesis):</li>
<li>Intramembranous</li>
<li>Endochondral</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intramembranous-ossification">Intramembranous ossification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intramembranous-ossification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Intramembranous ossification occurs in the connective tissue of the primary (membrane) bones.</li>
<li>The future bones are first formed as connective tissue membranes, that are replaced with bony tissue. Bones formed in this manner are called intramembranous bones. They include certain flat bones of the skull and some of the irregular bones.</li>
<li>The osteoblasts migrate to the membranes and deposit bony matrix around themselves.</li>
<li>As a result of osteoblastic activity appear points (centers) or nuclei of ossification.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="endochondral-ossification">Endochondral ossification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endochondral-ossification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Endochondral ossification involves the replacement of hyaline cartilage with bony tissue. Most of the bones of the skeleton are formed in this manner. These bones are called <strong>endochondral bones</strong>. In this process, the future bones are first formed as hyaline cartilage models</p>
<p>NB. Bone ossification is the process of bone formation and this process begins between the sixth and seventh weeks of embryonic development and continues until about the age of 25; although this varies slightly based on the individual.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">assignment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Examples of long, short, sessamoid, irregular, flat bones</li>
<li>Types of cartilage</li>
<li>Describe bone injury healing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>By the end of the lesson the learner will be able to:</li>
<li>Define bone injury</li>
<li>List the types of bone healing</li>
<li>Describe bone injury healing process</li>
<li>Assessment of orthopedic patient-history taking, physical examination, muscle strength testing</li>
</ul>
<p>BONE INJURY HEALING PROCESS</p>
<p>• BONE INJURY- also called bone fracture, occurs when a force exerted against a bone is stronger than a bone can bear</p>
<p>Bone injury healing process aims at restoring the damaged bone to its pre-injury state and cellular composition</p>
<ul>
<li>They are 2 main types of bone healing</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>primary bone healing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>secondary bone healing</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Primary bone healing- its an intramembranous bone healing that occurs through the haversian remodelling</li>
<li>Secondary bone healing- occurs in non rigid fixation modalities such as braces, external fixation, plates. It occurs via endochondral bone healing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-bone-healing-process">Stages of bone healing process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-bone-healing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hematoma formation</li>
<li>Granulation tissue formation</li>
<li>Bony callus formation</li>
<li>Bone remodelling</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stages-of-healing-bone-fracture">Stages Of Healing Bone Fracture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-healing-bone-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9294b4ae.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hematoma-formation">HEMATOMA FORMATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hematoma-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hematoma Formation: (Immediately after the fracture)</li>
<li>This forms the key step in fracture healing. The blood vessels supplying the bone and periosteum are disrupted during the fracture, causing a hematoma to form at the fracture site, which is rich in hematopoietic cells. The hematoma clots and forms the temporary frame for subsequent healing.</li>
<li>Macrophages, neutrophils, and platelets release pro-inflammatory cytokines such as tumor necrosis factor-alpha (TNF-α), bone morphogenetic proteins (BMPs), platelet-derived growth factors (PDGF), transforming growth factor beta (TGF-Beta), vascular endothelial growth factor (VEGF) and interleukins (IL-1, IL-6, IL-10, IL-11, IL 12, IL-23). These cytokines further stimulate essential cellular biology at the fracture site.</li>
</ul>
<p>Granulation Tissue Formation (Primary or fibrocartilaginous callus): (Within two weeks) This provides provisional stability.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Platelets are recruited to the fracture site. Among the products secreted by platelets are fibronectin (FN), platelet-derived growth factor (PDGF), and transforming growth factor-β (TGF-β), which collectively trigger an inflammatory response. Subsequently, other mesenchymal cells and inflammatory cells are recruited to the fracture site, such as fibroblasts and endothelial cells, with resultant fibrin-rich granulation tissue formation and angiogenesis. The granulation tissue withstands the greatest strain prior to failure during the healing process.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>Bony Callus Formation (If bone ends are not in contact, then a soft bridging callus forms):</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The endosteum and periosteum serve as primary sources for the Fibroblasts involved in fracture healing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The fibroblasts play a pivotal role by secreting the matrix constituents such as collagen, elastic and mesh fibers, and glycoproteins.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fibroblasts differentiate into osteoblasts guided by various bone morphogenic proteins (BMPs) and fibroblast growth factors (FGFs) released by the body at the fracture site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>With resultant increased levels of alkaline phosphatase (ALP), total calcium content, and osteogenic marker genes encoding for integrin-binding sialoprotein (IBSP), runt-related transcription factor 2 (Runx2), and osteoblast-associated transcription factors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cartilaginous (soft) callus begins to undergo endochondral ossification, and a medullary callus further supports the bridging soft callus. RANK-L is expressed, stimulating further differentiation of chondroblasts, chondroclasts, osteoblasts, and osteoclasts. As a result, the cartilaginous callus is resorbed and begins to calcify. Subperiosteally, woven bone continues to be laid down. The newly formed blood vessels continue to proliferate, allowing further migration of mesenchymal stem cells. At the end of this phase, a hard, calcified callus of immature bone forms. Bone callus formation is dependent upon appropriate relative motion between fracture fragments.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d1d42f47.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bone Remodelling (Continues for months to years after clinical union)</p>
<ul>
<li>This involves a complex interaction of signaling pathways, including BMP, fibroblast growth factor (FGF), parathyroid hormone-related peptide (PTHrP), and Indian hedgehog (Ihh). All of which are involved somehow in the differentiation of the appendicular skeleton.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-affecting-bone-healing">Factors affecting bone healing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-bone-healing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Systemic</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Age younger persons heal faster than aged people</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutrition</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Systemic diseases e.g. osteoporosis, diabetes and immunosuppression</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hormonal disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Local variables</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Types of bone. Cancellous bone has more blood supply</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Degree of trauma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vascular injury</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Degree of immobilization</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Site of fracture: intraarticular fractures communicate with synovial fluid which contain collageneses which retard bone healing and bone movement at this site disrupts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Separation of bone ends (degree of reduction)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Presence of local infection and other local pathology</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="asessment-of-orthopedic-patient">ASESSMENT OF ORTHOPEDIC PATIENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#asessment-of-orthopedic-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>HISTORY TAKING</li>
<li>PHYSICAL EXAMINATION</li>
<li>MUSCLE STRENGTH TESING</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="patient-history">PATIENT HISTORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patient-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A complete medical and injury history should be taken and written to ensure reliability</li>
<li>Often the examiner can make the diagnosis by simply listening to the patient</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="typical-complaints-symptoms">Typical Complaints (Symptoms)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#typical-complaints-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Stiffness</li>
<li>Swelling</li>
<li>Deformity</li>
<li>Weakness</li>
<li>Instability</li>
<li>Change in sensibility</li>
<li>Loss of function</li>
</ul>
<p>In any musculoskeletal assessment, the examiner should seek answers to the following pertinent questions;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>What is the patient's age and sex?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What is the patient's occupation?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Why has the patient come for help?
(history of the present illness or chief complaint)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Was there any inciting trauma (macrotrauma) or repetitive activity (microtrauma)?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Was the onset of the problem slow or sudden?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where are the symptoms that bother the patient?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where was the pain or other symptoms when the patient first had the complaint?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Has the pain moved or spread?</li>
</ul>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>What are the exact movements or activities that cause pain?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How long has the problem existed? What are the duration and frequency of the symptoms?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has the condition occurred before?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has there been an injury to another part of the kinetic chain as well?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are the intensity, duration, or frequency of pain or other symptoms increasing?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is the pain constant, periodic, episodic (occurring with certain activities), or occasional?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is the pain associated with rest? Activity? Certain postures? Visceral function? Time of day?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What type or quality of pain is exhibited?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pain-descriptions-and-related-structures">Pain Descriptions and Related Structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain-descriptions-and-related-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type of Pain</th><th>Structure</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Cramping, dull, aching</td><td>Muscle</td></tr><tr><td>Dull, aching</td><td>Ligament, joint capsule</td></tr><tr><td>Sharp, shooting</td><td>Nerve root</td></tr><tr><td>Sharp, bright, lightning-like</td><td>Nerve</td></tr><tr><td>Burning, pressure-like, stinging, aching</td><td>Sympathetic nerve</td></tr><tr><td>Deep, nagging, dull</td><td>Bone</td></tr><tr><td>Sharp, severe, intolerable</td><td>Fracture</td></tr><tr><td>Throbbing, diffuse</td><td>Vasculature</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Assessment for pain</p>
<p>• Site - Where is the pain? Or the maximal site of the pain.</p>
<p>• Onset - When did the pain start, and was it sudden or gradual? Include also whether if it is progressive or regressive.</p>
<p>• Character - What is the pain like? An ache? Stabbing?</p>
<p>• Radiation - Does the pain radiate anywhere? (See also Radiation.)</p>
<p>• Associations - Any other signs or symptoms associated with the pain?</p>
<p>• Time course - Does the pain follow any pattern?</p>
<p>• Exacerbating/Relieving factors - Does anything change the pain?</p>
<p>• Severity - How bad is the pain?</p>
<p>SOCRATES</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-for-pain">Management for pain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-for-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medications – Analgesics, NSAIDs, COX</li>
<li>Physiotherapy – useful with chronic musculoskeletal conditions or where there has been long periods of muscle inactivity.</li>
<li>Distraction – music, play, TV, conversation. Used to shift attention away from the pain &amp; onto other activities.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="16">
<li>
<p>What types of sensations does the patient feel, and where are these abnormal sensations?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Does a joint exhibit locking, unlocking, twinges, instability, or giving way?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has the patient experienced any bilateral spinal cord symptoms, fainting, or drop attacks?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are there any changes in the color of the limb?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has the patient been experiencing any life or economic stresses?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Does the patient have any chronic or serious systemic illnesses or adverse social habits?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is there anything in the family or developmental history that may be related?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has the patient undergone an x-ray examination or other imaging techniques?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has the patient been receiving analgesic, steroid, or any other medication? If so, for how long?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Does the patient have a history of surgery or past/present illness?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-examination">PHYSICAL EXAMINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In physical examination of a patient you mainly use inspection and palpation</li>
<li>Inspection- Assess for the presence of the following: Skin changes (e.g., erythema, pigmentation, scars) Changes in shape and/or alignment of the body part (e.g., due to edema, atrophy, lumps) Abnormal position (e.g., limb contractures, scoliosis)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palpation">Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Local temperature</li>
<li>Crepitus in the joints and soft tissues</li>
<li>Swelling</li>
<li>Painful areas, tenderness</li>
<li>Tonus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="palpation">Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Note any local heat any tenderness, whether localized or diffuse</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e95f216c.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-8cf426be.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<p>Note any joint crepitus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="auscultation-and-percussion">Auscultation and Percussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auscultation-and-percussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Are needed in the chest and abdomen damages to determinate:</p>
<ul>
<li>the blood level in the cavities;</li>
<li>presence of pneumothorax;</li>
<li>changes of breathing;</li>
<li>function of intestines</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="movement">Movement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#movement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Determination of the range of motion in the joints</li>
<li>Movements in an abnormal range or plane</li>
<li>The cause of abnormal range of motion (pain, contraction, deformity)</li>
</ul>
<p>Movement of a joint is either <strong>active</strong> (i.e. inducted by the patient) or <strong>passive</strong> (i.e. inducted by the examiner).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="measuring-of-the-range-of-motion-in-the-joints">Measuring of the range of motion in the joints<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measuring-of-the-range-of-motion-in-the-joints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a59ec5d4.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a978b1cf.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-4337bf2e.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p>Use of the goniometer to measure the different joint motion.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-99b3e6bc.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p>The neutral position from which joint measurement is performed</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neutral-position">Neutral position:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neutral-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>the limbs extended with the feet dorsi-flexed to 90°, the upper limbs midway between pronation and supination with the arms flexed to 90° at the elbow.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-procedures">DIAGNOSTIC PROCEDURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-procedures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1c88d5e4.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-801fbc73.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="arthroscopy">Arthroscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arthroscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Arthroscopy is primarily used to help diagnose joint problems. This procedure, most commonly associated with knee and shoulder problems, allows accurate examination and diagnosis of damaged joint ligaments, surfaces, and other related joint structures.</p>
<p>Arthrocentesis (also called joint aspiration) is a procedure where a doctor uses a needle to take fluid out of a joint. Joints are where two bones meet. They allow our bodies to move. The hips, knees, ankles, elbows, shoulders, and knuckles are all joint</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d535055e.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="muscle-strength-testing">MUSCLE STRENGTH TESTING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#muscle-strength-testing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-muscle-strength">WHAT IS MUSCLE STRENGTH?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-muscle-strength" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>According to the AMERICAN COUNCIL OF EXERCISE, muscular strength is the maximal force a muscle or a muscle group can exert during a contraction.</p>
<p>Factors related to muscle strength are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The size of the muscle fibers</li>
<li>The ability of the nerves to activate the muscle fibers</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="terms-related-to-muscle-strength">TERMS RELATED TO MUSCLE STRENGTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terms-related-to-muscle-strength" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Power: The combination of muscular force and speed of movement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>ENDURANCE: The ability of the muscles to exert force against resistance over a sustained period of time or repetitions is known as muscular endurance.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="muscle-strength-testing">Muscle strength testing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#muscle-strength-testing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In muscular strength testing we assess the muscular strength of a patient as part of objective assessment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purpose">Purpose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Diagnostic</li>
<li>Examine the improvement or deterioration of patients status overtime</li>
<li>Determine the extent of strength loss</li>
<li>Help in formulating a nursing diagnosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="methods-of-muscle-strength">Methods of muscle strength<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-muscle-strength" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mechanically/ instrumentally</li>
<li>manually</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mechanical-instrumental-muscle-testing">Mechanical/ instrumental muscle testing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanical-instrumental-muscle-testing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this the following instruments are used;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>☑ Strain gauge</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>☑ Cable tensiometer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>HAND HELD DYNAMOMETER OR GRIP STRENGTH DYNAMOMETER</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>MODIFIED SPHYGMOMAMOMETER</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>PINCH METER</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cable-tensiometer">CABLE TENSIOMETER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cable-tensiometer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In cable tensiometer, two cables will be there in which one end of the cable is attached to some fixed or stable object and the other end is attached to a limb segment. As the cable is pulled, it presses the tensiometer's bar which is connected to the gauge that measures in relative units.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ffad04c6.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>STRAIN GAUGE</p>
<p>Strain gauges are made of electro conductive material. Strain gauge devices are less often used for muscle evaluation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="click-icon-to-add-picture">Click icon to add picture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#click-icon-to-add-picture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A strain gauge is an electrical sensor, they are used to measure and monitor strain. They are sometimes used as part of different sensors; load cells, pressure transducers and others. The resistance of a strain gauge changes when force is applied and this change will give a different electrical output.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-14ecfd1e.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ea52869e.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hand-held-dynamometer-or-grip-strength-dynamometer">HAND HELD DYNAMOMETER OR GRIP STRENGTH DYNAMOMETER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-held-dynamometer-or-grip-strength-dynamometer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mainly used for measuring strength of the hand and forearm muscles.</p>
<p>Maximum grip strength is the measure of three trails.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b40a01f7.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2214be69.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="modified-sphygomamometer">MODIFIED SPHYGOMAMOMETER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#modified-sphygomamometer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Inflate the cuff up to 20mmHg</li>
<li>Then squeeze the cuff and note the readings</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9376b13d.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1e64b50e.jpeg" alt="img-24.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-4f30ad7d.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<p>.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-600bf3a4.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pinch-meter">PINCH METER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pinch-meter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is used to assess strength of fingers.</p>
<ol>
<li>TIP PINCH- thumb and index finger</li>
<li>LATERAL/KEY PINCH-thumb pad and lateral aspect of the index finger</li>
<li>PALMAR PINCH- thumb, index and middle finger</li>
</ol>
<p>Average of 3 trials for each pinch position is taken.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-92e63bc1.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="manual-muscle-testing">MANUAL MUSCLE TESTING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#manual-muscle-testing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Manual muscle testing is the most popular way to test strength. The therapist will push the body parts in specific directions while the patient will resist the pressure.</p>
<p>The Oxford scale OR MRC Scale is commonly used by physiotherapists to manually assess muscle strength. According to the Oxford scale, muscle strength is graded 0 to 5. The grades are summarized below:</p>
<p>0/5</p>
<p>A 0/5 score means that the patient is unable to create any visible or noticeable contraction in a specific muscle. This occurs when a muscle is paralyzed, such as after a stroke, spinal cord injury, or cervical or lumbar radiculopathy. Sometimes pain can prevent a muscle from contracting at all.</p>
<p>1/5</p>
<p>A grade of 1/5 occurs when muscle contraction is noted but no movement occurs. A small flicker of muscle contraction may be palpated, or felt, during testing.</p>
<p>2/5</p>
<p>This muscle-strength grade is assigned when the muscle can contract but cannot move the body part fully against gravity. When gravity is reduced or eliminated during a change in body position, the muscle is able to move the body part through its full range of motion.</p>
<p>3/5</p>
<p>A 3/5 grade means that the patient is able to fully contract the muscle and move the body part through its full range of motion against the force of gravity. But when resistance is applied, the muscle is unable to maintain the contraction.</p>
<p>4/5</p>
<p>A 4/5 grade indicates that the muscle is able to contract and provide some resistance, but when the therapist presses on the body part with maximum force, the muscle is unable to maintain the contraction.</p>
<p>5/5</p>
<p>This means the muscle is functioning normally and is able to maintain its position even when maximum resistance is applied.</p>
<p>Occasionally the therapist may grade the muscle strength in half increments, using the + or - sign. The use of these incremental grades is subjective, which makes them unreliable.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>0</th><th>0</th><th>No visible or palpable contraction</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Trace</td><td>I</td><td>1 Visible or palpable contraction (No ROM)</td></tr><tr><td>Poor-</td><td></td><td>2- Partial ROM, gravity eliminated</td></tr><tr><td>Poor</td><td>II</td><td>2 Full ROM, gravity eliminated</td></tr><tr><td>Poor+</td><td></td><td>2+ Gravity eliminated/slight resistance or &lt; 1/2 range against gravity</td></tr><tr><td>Fair-</td><td></td><td>3- &gt; 1/2 but &lt; Full ROM, against gravity</td></tr><tr><td>Fair</td><td>III</td><td>3 Full ROM against gravity</td></tr><tr><td>Fair+</td><td></td><td>3+ Full ROM against gravity, slight resistance</td></tr><tr><td>Good-</td><td></td><td>4- Full ROM against gravity, mild resistance</td></tr><tr><td>Good</td><td>IV</td><td>4 Full ROM against gravity, moderate resistance</td></tr><tr><td>Good+</td><td></td><td>4+ Full ROM against gravity, almost full resistance</td></tr><tr><td>Normal</td><td>V</td><td>Normal, maximal resistance</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="resisted-isometric-contraction">RESISTED ISOMETRIC CONTRACTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resisted-isometric-contraction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Isometric muscle testing is commonly performed by therapists to test the strength and determine whether an injury or illness has affected it. It can be used test the strength and determine whether the workout routine is effectively helping you to get stronger.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="orthopedic-trauma-and-injuries">ORTHOPEDIC TRAUMA AND INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orthopedic-trauma-and-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this topic the learner should be able to: describe, state the causes and manage the different orthopedic trauma and injuries</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fractures">FRACTURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fractures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>DEFINITION</li>
<li>What is a fracture?</li>
<li>A fracture is a partial or complete break in the bone. When a fracture happens, it's classified as either open or closed:</li>
<li>Open fracture (also called compound fracture): The bone pokes through the skin and can be seen, or a deep wound exposes the bone through the skin.</li>
<li>Closed fracture (also called simple fracture). The bone is broken, but the skin is intact.</li>
<li>A fracture occurs when force exerted against a bone is stronger than the bone can structurally withstand.</li>
</ul>
<p>Fractures have a variety of names. Here is a listing of the common types that may happen:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Greenstick. This is an incomplete fracture. A portion of the bone is broken, causing the other side to bend.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Transverse. The break is in a straight line across the bone.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spiral. The break spirals around the bone; common in a twisting injury.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oblique. The break is diagonal across the bone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compression. The bone is crushed. This causes the broken bone to be wider or flatter in appearance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Comminuted. The bone has broken into three or more pieces and fragments are present at the fracture site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Segmental. The same bone is fractured in two places, so there is a "floating" piece of bone.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-681df695.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg">
Types of Fracture</p>
<p>Transverse Linear Oblique, nondisplaced Oblique, displaced Spiral Greenstick Comminuted</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-causes-fractures">What causes fractures?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-causes-fractures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fractures most often happen when more force is applied to the bone than the bone can take. Bones are weakest when they are twisted.</li>
<li>Bone fractures can be caused by falls, trauma, or as a result of a direct blow or kick to the body.</li>
<li>Overuse or repetitive motions can tire muscles and put more pressure on the bone. This causes stress fractures. This is more common in athletes.</li>
<li>Fractures can also be caused by diseases that weaken the bone, such as osteoporosis or cancer in the bones.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-are-the-symptoms-of-a-fracture">What are the symptoms of a fracture?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-symptoms-of-a-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The following are the most common symptoms of a fracture. However, each person may experience symptoms differently. Symptoms of a broken or fractured bone may include:</li>
<li>Sudden pain</li>
<li>Trouble using or moving the injured area or nearby joints</li>
<li>Swelling</li>
<li>Obvious deformity</li>
<li>Warmth, bruising, or redness</li>
</ul>
<p>COMPLICATIONS</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Some complications (such as blood vessel and nerve damage, compartment syndrome, fat embolism, and infections) occur during the first hours or days after the injury.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Others (such as problems with joints and healing) develop over time.(Osteonecrosis)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compartment syndrome is a condition in which increased pressure within one of the body's anatomical compartments results in insufficient blood supply to tissue within that space. There are two main types: acute and chronic. Compartments of the leg or arm are most commonly involved.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-care-acute-compartment-syndrome">Emergency Care - Acute Compartment Syndrome<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-care-acute-compartment-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Within 4 to 6 hr after the onset of acute compartment syndrome, neuromuscular damage is irreversible; the limb can become useless within 24 to 48 hr.</li>
<li>Monitor compartment pressures.</li>
<li>Fasciotomy may be performed to relieve pressure.</li>
<li>Pack and dress the wound after fasciotomy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-is-a-fracture-diagnosed">How is a fracture diagnosed?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-is-a-fracture-diagnosed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In addition to a complete medical history (including asking how the injury happened) and physical exam, tests used for a fracture may include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>X-ray. A diagnostic test which uses invisible electromagnetic energy beams to make pictures of internal tissues, bones, and organs on film</li>
<li>Magnetic resonance imaging (MRI). An imaging test that uses large magnets, radiofrequencies, and a computer to produce detailed pictures of structures within the body.</li>
<li>Computed tomography scan (also called a CT or CAT scan). This is an imaging test that uses X-rays and a computer to make detailed images of the body. A CT scan shows details of the bones, muscles, fat, and organs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-fractures">MANAGEMENT OF FRACTURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-fractures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Assessment</p>
<ul>
<li>Five P⁵</li>
<li>pain,</li>
<li>pulse,</li>
<li>pallor,</li>
<li>Paresthesia—the feeling of tingling, numbness or “pins and needles.”</li>
<li>paralysis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-fractures">MANAGEMENT OF FRACTURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-fractures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fracture reduction</li>
<li>Immobilisation</li>
<li>traction</li>
<li>Rehabilitation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reduction">Reduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Aim</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>replace the bone fragments to as near as normal anatomical position as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open reduction. This is a surgical method</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Closed reduction. Here manipulation is used without viewing the fractures</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>manual reduction of distal radius fractures is shown in Figure</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1985fd7d.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg">
Step 1: stretch the fracture part
Step 2: move the distal fragment</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a6e63678.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg">
Step 3: maintain the position of flexion and ulnar deviation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immobilisation">Immobilisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immobilisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Aim</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>prevent movement of injured parts already reduced by the above methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Methods</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>External devices e.g. splints, plaster casts, external fixation devices or traction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Internal devices inserted during open reduction e.g. screws, nails, plates</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="immobilization-techniques">IMMOBILIZATION TECHNIQUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immobilization-techniques" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-eb8dc983.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b6b970f5.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg">
Chest arm bandage</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3a31ca50.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg">
Triangular sling</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b29d4019.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg"></p>
