<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="internal-fixation">Internal fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internal-fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Advantage</li>
<li>allows direct visualisation of fracture of the surrounding tissues</li>
<li>Disadvantage</li>
<li>Requires anaesthesia</li>
<li>There is the risk of infection</li>
<li>Indications</li>
<li>compound fractures</li>
<li>Fractures with fragments widely separated</li>
<li>Fractures with soft tissue interposed between</li>
<li>Fractures with extensive neurovascular injury</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a974da97.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1c081f12.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6733cbe2.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-afb460d5.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<p>To stabilize a long bone fracture, a plate and screws outside the bone or a rod inside the bone may be used</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-0bcde939.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ab6b771d.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-8e2c8d60.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg">
Intramedullary rod
*ADAM</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-patient-after-orif">Care of patient after ORIF<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-patient-after-orif" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Goals</li>
<li>Complete union in 4-6 months</li>
<li>Prevention of complications, deformities and contractures</li>
<li>Restoration of weight bearing ambulation</li>
<li>Relieve pain, discomfort and fear</li>
<li>Restoration and maintenance of optimal physiological function</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pre-operatively</li>
<li>Investigations X-ray, Hb, GXM,</li>
<li>Assessment for any underlying medical conditions</li>
<li>Vital signs TPR and BP</li>
<li>Routine pre-operative care</li>
<li>Post-operatively</li>
</ul>
<p>Apart from the general post-operative care the nurse should:</p>
<ul>
<li>Comparison of peripheral pulses between affected and unaffected extremities</li>
<li>Assessment of mobility and self care needs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-and-interventions-for-patients-with-internal-fixation">Complications and interventions For patients with internal fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-and-interventions-for-patients-with-internal-fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Deep venous thrombosis</li>
<li>Clot prophylaxis through use of low dose anti-coagulants for some clients</li>
<li>Pressure ulcers</li>
<li>Turning schedule and care of pressure areas</li>
<li>Acute confusion</li>
<li>Managing pain, metabolic imbalances and psychological support</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="external-fixation">External fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Indication</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>extensive soft tissue and bone injury where an internal device may not be used i.e used to keep fractured bones stabilized and in alignment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The device can be adjusted externally to ensure the bones remain in an optimal position during the healing process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disadvantage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Requires general anaesthesia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advantages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allows client use contiguous joints while affected areas remain immobilized</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6ae795ce.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-cd7b121c.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<p>Screws are placed into the bone above and below the fracture, and a device is attached to the screws from outside the skin, where it may be adjusted to realign the bone</p>
<p>ADAM</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-da1bc529.jpeg" alt="img-44.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="external-fixation">External fixation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-fixation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing management</li>
<li>The main nursing concerns are</li>
<li>Neurological deficits</li>
<li>Compartment syndrome</li>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Risk of infection at the pin sites</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prophylactic antibiotics (48-72 hours prior)</li>
<li>Observe for loose pins or ‘tenting’ of skin</li>
<li>Correct use of ambulatory aids to avoid stress on the fracture site</li>
<li>Pain management by both analgesics and other techniques such as distraction and massage</li>
<li>Issues of body image as fixation affects body image should be addressed</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="traction">Traction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>involves a steady pull on a body part and is both reduction and immobilization to maintain fractures apart but allowing sufficient contact for healing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goal">Goal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To reduce a fracture</li>
<li>Maintain alignment</li>
<li>Overcome muscle spasm</li>
<li>Correct deformities</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-traction">Types of Traction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-traction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Skin traction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the pull is transmitted to the skin on the fractured bone weights are used to maintain traction and the traction force must be maintained throughout the initial healing stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skeletal traction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the force is directly applied to the bone by use of pulls weights are used to maintain traction and the traction force must be maintained throughout the initial healing stage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skeletal traction</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b221110c.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Skin traction</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ed2d20bf.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="skin-vs-skeletal-traction">SKIN vs SKELETAL TRACTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin-vs-skeletal-traction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Skin Traction</th><th>Skeletal Traction</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Required for force</td><td>Mild</td><td>Moderate/ severe</td></tr><tr><td>Age used</td><td>Children</td><td>Adults</td></tr><tr><td>Applied with</td><td>Adhesive tape</td><td>Steinmann, K-wire</td></tr><tr><td>Commonly</td><td>Below knee</td><td>Upper tibia</td></tr><tr><td>Weight permitted</td><td>2-3 kg</td><td>Up to 20 kgm</td></tr><tr><td>Duration</td><td>Short</td><td>Long</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="plaster">Plaster<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plaster" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>external fixation device which is applied over skin</li>
<li>The skin should be intact, clean and well padded before a cast is applied to avoid risks of infection.</li>
<li>Casts are molded over the affected body part after closed reduction has been done</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-patient-with-a-cast">Nursing care for patient with a cast<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-patient-with-a-cast" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Patient Education</li>
<li>explain the procedure to the patient and the extent of the immobilisation.</li>
<li>explain the care of cast to the patient and when it will be removed.</li>
<li>Instruct patient not to insert sharp objects in to the cast to avoid injury in the skin.</li>
<li>Skin Care</li>
<li>Inspect skin around the cast edges for redness or irritation.</li>
<li>After cast removal, skin should be washed thoroughly and oiled.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mobilisation</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Weight bearing is at the discretion of the physician. The patient can ambulate on crutches.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positioning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After cast application, position limb elevated on a pillow to decrease oedema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observe limb for colour changes and sensation. If the patient experiences tingling sensations, the cast is too tight and should be removed</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Inspect skin around the cast edges for redness or irritation.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>After removal, skin should be washed thoroughly and oiled.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mobilisation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight bearing is at the discretion of the physician. The patient can ambulate on crutches.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positioning</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After cast application, position limb elevated on a pillow to decrease oedema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observe limb for colour changes and sensation. If the patient experiences tingling sensations, the cast is too tight and should be removed</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="polytrauma">POLYTRAUMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#polytrauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Poly-trauma means a syndrome of multiple injuries with systemic traumatic reactions which may lead to dysfunction or failure of remote organs and vital systems.</p>
<p>1/29/2017</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Polytrauma is a significant injury in at least two of the following six body regions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Head, neck and cervical spine</li>
<li>Face</li>
<li>Chest and thoracic spine</li>
<li>Abdomen and lumbar spine</li>
<li>Limbs and bony pelvis</li>
<li>External (skin) Significant</li>
</ul>
<p>injury in AIS ≥ 3</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abbreviated-injury-score-ais">Abbreviated injury score AIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abbreviated-injury-score-ais" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>&gt;=3 injury severity score ISS</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Region</th><th>Injury Description</th><th>AIS</th><th>Square Top Three</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Head &amp; Neck</td><td>Cerebral Contusion</td><td>3</td><td>9</td></tr><tr><td>Face</td><td>No Injury</td><td>0</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Chest</td><td>Flail Chest</td><td>4</td><td>16</td></tr><tr><td>Abdomen</td><td>Minor Contusion of Liver</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Complex Rupture Spleen</td><td>2</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>25</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Extremity</td><td>Fractured femur</td><td>3</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>External</td><td>No Injury</td><td>0</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Injury Severity Score:</td><td></td><td></td><td>50</td></tr><tr><td>AIS Score</td><td>Injury</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Minor</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Moderate</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Serious</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Severe</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>5</td><td>Critical</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>6</td><td>Survivable</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-golden-hour">The Golden Hour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-golden-hour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>originated by R Adams Cowley</li>
<li>first sixty minutes after the occurrence of multi- system trauma</li>
<li>victim's chances of survival are <strong>greatest</strong> if they receive definitive care in the OR within the first hour after a severe injury</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology-of-polytrauma">Etiology of polytrauma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology-of-polytrauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>RTA</li>
<li>Fall from height (blunt or penetrating injury)</li>
<li>Airplane crashes, train derailment</li>
<li>Assault</li>
<li>Blast</li>
<li>Thermal, chemical injury</li>
</ul>

<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-4a69d38a.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology-of-polytrauma">Pathophysiology Of Polytrauma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-polytrauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Is complex phenomenon aiming at the restoration of homeostasis and preservation of life</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-71408117.jpeg" alt="img-51.jpeg"></p>
<p>Host defense response during polytrauma (two hit theory)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="type-of-shock-in-polytraumatized-patient">Type of shock in polytraumatized patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-of-shock-in-polytraumatized-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Hemorrhagic shock
&gt; duo to loss blood volume, diagnosis based on vital sign and examination characterized by hypotension, tachycardia and cold skin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neurogenic shock
&gt; duo to spinal cord injury that causes distribution of sympathetic outflow to heart and blood vessels characterized by hypotension, bradycardia, warm skin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypoxic shock</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Septic shock</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>READ ON THE MANAGEMENT/ CARE FOR POLYTRAUMATIZED PATIENT</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amputation">AMPUTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amputation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Amputation is a process where a part of the limb is removed through one of more bones.</li>
<li>Disarticulation – where a part is removed through a joint</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-for-amputation">Causes for amputation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-for-amputation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>PVD</li>
<li>Injuries / trauma – RTA, gunshots</li>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Tumors</li>
<li>Congenital anomalies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-amputation">Types of amputation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-amputation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>guillotine or open amputation-
Secondary closure
Plastic repair
Revision of the stump
Re-amputation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>closed amputation – here the skin is closed primarily.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Haematoma</li>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Skin flap necrosis</li>
<li>Deformities of joints</li>
<li>Neuroma</li>
<li>Phantom sensations</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="goals-of-management-for-a-client-who-has-undergone-amputation">GOALS OF MANAGEMENT FOR A CLIENT WHO HAS UNDERGONE AMPUTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals-of-management-for-a-client-who-has-undergone-amputation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goals-of-management">Goals of management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals-of-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pain management</li>
<li>Psychological counseling</li>
<li>Dressing</li>
<li>Skin care</li>
<li>Prevention of deformity, maintain ROM, strengthening</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">ASSIGNMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Read on: nerve injuries, soft tissue injuries, vascular injuries and sport injuries focusing on: ( the causes, types and the management</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="orthopedic-conditions">ORTHOPEDIC CONDITIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#orthopedic-conditions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>infection of the bone and
joints</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bone-tuberculosis">BONE TUBERCULOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bone-tuberculosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Spine – Pott’s spine (50% of all cases of skeletal Tuberculosis)</li>
<li>Joints – Tubercular arthritis:</li>
<li>Hip Joint</li>
<li>Knee joint and Triple deformity</li>
<li>Shoulder joint and Caries Sicca</li>
<li>Elbow joint</li>
<li>Wrist and Carpus</li>
<li>Sacroiliac joints</li>
<li>Long and flat bones – Tubercular osteomyelitis</li>
<li>Short bones – Tubercular dactylitis (spina ventosa)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tuberculosis-of-spine">TUBERCULOSIS OF SPINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tuberculosis-of-spine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>first described by Sir Percival Pott in 1779, hence the name Potts disease</li>
<li>Usually two continuous vertebrae involved but several vertebrae maybe affected, skip lesions and solitary vertebral involvement may occur</li>
<li>skip lesions — 4 -10 % of cases.</li>
<li>12% cases - has associated other osteo-articular tuberculous involvement</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">CLINICAL FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>any age group; majority &lt;30 years</li>
<li>Male=female</li>
<li>Rare in the 1st year of life but when it occurs, tends to be more severe</li>
<li>Constitutional symptoms:</li>
<li>Malaise</li>
<li>Loss of weight/appetite</li>
<li>Night sweats</li>
<li>Evening rise of temperature</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">CLINICAL FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Specific Symptoms:</li>
<li>Pain/Night cries</li>
<li>Stiffness/spasm of vertebral muscles</li>
<li>Localized/Persistent backache</li>
<li>Deformity</li>
<li>Restricted ROM</li>
<li>Enlarged lymph nodes</li>
<li>Abscess and sinuses</li>
<li>Neurological deficit</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neurological-complications">NEUROLOGICAL COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurological-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>10-30% cases – Neurological deficit</li>
<li>Age: 1st 3 decades</li>
<li>Disease below L1 vertebrae rarely causes Paraplegia</li>
<li>Highest incidence of paraplegia: TB of lower thoracic vertebrae</li>
<li>Commonest pathology for non traumatic paraplegia in developing countries still remains Tuberculosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">PREDISPOSING FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general">GENERAL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Malnutrition</li>
<li>Poor sanitation</li>
<li>Living in crowded areas</li>
<li>Close contact with TB patients</li>
<li>Repeated pregnancies</li>
<li>Exanthematous fevers</li>
<li>Immuno deficiency states</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>LOCAL - TRAUMA, MOVEMENTS, INCREASED</li>
<li>LOADS, DECREASED VASCULARITY</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="osteomyelitis">OSTEOMYELITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#osteomyelitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Osteomyelitis is a serious infection of the bone that can be either acute or chronic. It is an inflammatory process involving the bone and its structures caused by pyogenic organisms that spread through the bloodstream, fractures, or surgery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Osteomyelitis occurs when bacteria from nearby infected tissue or an open wound circulate in your blood and settle in bone, where they multiply. Staphylococcus aureus bacteria (staph infection) typically cause osteomyelitis. Sometimes, a fungus or other germ causes a bone infection</li>
</ul>
<p>Symptoms</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Signs and symptoms of osteomyelitis include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fever</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Swelling, warmth and redness over the area of the infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pain in the area of the infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fatigue</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causative-organisms">CAUSATIVE ORGANISMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causative-organisms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Staphylococcus aureus (more than 50% of bone infections)</li>
<li>Gram-positive organisms streptococci and enterococci</li>
<li>Gram-negative bacteria- pseudomonas</li>
<li>Salmonella</li>
<li>E. coli</li>
<li>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</li>
<li>Neisseria gonorrhoea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">PATHOPHYSIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a41a61aa.jpeg" alt="img-52.jpeg"></p>
<p>Risk factors</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Your bones are normally resistant to infection, but this protection lessens as you get older. Other factors that can make your bones more vulnerable to osteomyelitis may include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Recent injury or orthopedic surgery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A severe bone fracture or a deep puncture wound gives bacteria a route to enter your bone or nearby tissue. A deep puncture wound, such as an animal bite or a nail piercing through a shoe, can also provide a pathway for infection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surgery to repair broken bones or replace worn joints also can accidentally open a path for germs to enter a bone. Implanted orthopedic hardware is a risk factor for infection.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Circulation disorders</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>When blood vessels are damaged or blocked, your body has trouble distributing the infection-fighting cells needed to keep a small infection from growing larger. What begins as a small cut can progress to a deep ulcer that may expose deep tissue and bone to infection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diseases that impair blood circulation include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poorly controlled diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Peripheral artery disease, often related to smoking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sickle cell disease</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Problems requiring intravenous lines or catheters</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>There are a number of conditions that require the use of medical tubing to connect the outside world with your internal organs. However, this tubing can also serve as a way for germs to get into your body, increasing your risk of an infection in general, which can lead to osteomyelitis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Examples of when this type of tubing might be used include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dialysis machine tubing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Urinary catheters</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Long-term intravenous tubing, sometimes called central lines</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>Conditions that impair the immune system</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If your immune system is affected by a medical condition or medication, you have a greater risk of osteomyelitis. Factors that may suppress your immune system include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cancer treatment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poorly controlled diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Needing to take corticosteroids or drugs called tumor necrosis factor inhibitors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Illicit drugs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>People who inject illegal drugs are more likely to develop osteomyelitis because they may use nonsterile needles and are less likely to sterilize their skin before injections.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="at-risk-patients">AT RISK PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#at-risk-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Older adults</li>
<li>Poorly nourished</li>
<li>Obese</li>
<li>Impaired immune system</li>
<li>Chronic illness (e.g. diabetes, rheumatoid arthritis)</li>
<li>Receiving long-term corticosteroid therapy or immunosuppressive agents</li>
<li>Intravenous drug users</li>
</ul>
<p>Complications</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Osteomyelitis complications may include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bone death (osteonecrosis). An infection in your bone can impede blood circulation within the bone, leading to bone death. Areas where bone has died need to be surgically removed for antibiotics to be effective.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Septic arthritis. Sometimes, infection within bones can spread into a nearby joint.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impaired growth. Normal growth in bones or joints in children may be affected if osteomyelitis occurs in the softer areas, called growth plates, at either end of the long bones of the arms and legs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skin cancer. If your osteomyelitis has resulted in an open sore that is draining pus, the surrounding skin is at higher risk of developing squamous cell cancer.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-osteomyelitis">MANAGEMENT OF OSTEOMYELITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-osteomyelitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">PREVENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Elective orthopaedic surgery should be postponed if the patient has a current infection (e.g. urinary tract infection, sore throat).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>During surgery, careful attention is paid to the surgical environment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prophylactic antibiotics, administered to achieve adequate tissue levels at the time of surgery and for 24 hours after surgery, are helpful.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Urinary catheters and drains are removed as soon as possible to decrease the incidence of hematogenous spread of infection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aseptic postoperative wound care reduces the incidence of superficial infections and osteomyelitis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prompt management of soft tissue infections reduces extension of infection to the bone or hematogenous spread.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When patients who have had joint replacement surgery undergo extensive dental procedures or other invasive procedures (e.g., cystoscopy), prophylactic antibiotics are recommended before the procedure.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">NURSING MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-assessment">Nursing assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Assess the <strong>sign and symptoms</strong>- localized pain, edema, erythema, fever, etc or recurrent drainage of an infected sinus with associated pain, edema and low-grade fever.</li>
<li>Assess for <strong>risk factors</strong>- older age, diabetes, long term corticosteroid therapy and a history of previous injury, infection, or orthopaedic surgery.</li>
<li>Assess the <strong>gait</strong> as it may be altered as the patient avoids pressure and movement of the area.</li>
<li>In acute hematogenous osteomyelitis, the patient exhibits <strong>generalized weakness due to the systemic reaction</strong> to the infection.</li>
<li>Assess for inflamed, markedly edematous, warm area that is tender, purulent drainage, elevated temperature, etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnosis">NURSING DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute pain related to inflammation and edema.</li>
<li>Impaired physical mobility related to pain, use of immobilization devices, and weight-bearing limitations.</li>
<li>Infection related to bone abscess formation.</li>
<li>Deficient knowledge related to the treatment regimen.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="arthritis">ARTHRITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arthritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Arthritis is the swelling and tenderness of one or more joints.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Types of arthritis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inflammatory arthritis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inflammation is a normal part of the body’s healing process. It tends to occur as a defense against viruses and bacteria or as a response to injuries such as burns.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Examples of inflammatory arthritis include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>RA</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>reactive arthritis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>ankylosing spondylitis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>psoriatic arthritis</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Degenerative or mechanical arthritis</p>
<p>-Degenerative or mechanical arthritis refers to a group of conditions that mainly involve damage to the cartilage that covers the ends of the bones.</p>
<p>Connective tissue disease (CTD)</p>
<p>• Connective tissues support, bind together, or separate other body tissues and organs. They include tendons, ligaments, and cartilage.</p>
<p>Examples of CTD include:</p>
<p>• SLE, or lupus</p>
<p>• scleroderma, or systemic sclerosis</p>
<p>• dermatomyositis</p>
<p>• Sjogren’s</p>
<ul>
<li>Infectious arthritis</li>
<li>A bacterium, virus, or fungus that enters a joint can sometimes cause inflammation.</li>
<li>Organisms that can infect joints include:</li>
<li>salmonella and shigella, which spread through food poisoning or contamination</li>
<li>chlamydia and gonorrhea, which are sexually transmitted diseases (STDs)</li>
<li>hepatitis C, which is a blood-to-blood infection that may be spread through shared needles or transfusions</li>
</ul>
<p>Metabolic arthritis</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Uric acid is a chemical created when the body breaks down substances called purines. Purines are found in human cells and several foods.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most uric acid dissolves in blood and travels to the kidneys. From there, it passes out of the body in urine. Some people have high uric acid levels because they either naturally produce more than they need or their body cannot clear the uric acid quickly enough.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uric acid builds up and accumulates in some people and forms needle-like crystals in the joint, resulting in sudden spikes of extreme joint pain or a gout attack.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gout can either come and go in episodes or become chronic if uric acid levels are not reduced.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Childhood arthritis</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This can refer to a number of types of arthritis. Juvenile idiopathic arthritis (JIA), also known as juvenile rheumatoid arthritis (JRA), is the most commonTrusted Source type.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arthritis in childhood can cause permanent damage to joints, and there is no cure. However, remission is possible, during which time the disease remains inactive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It may be due to immune system problems.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Septic arthritis is a joint inflammation that results from a bacterial or fungal infection. It commonly affects the knee and hip.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Symptoms of arthritis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pain: Pain from arthritis can be constant, or it may come and go. It may affect only one part or be felt in many parts of the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Swelling: In some types of arthritis, the skin over the affected joint becomes red and swollen and feels warm to the touch.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stiffness: Stiffness is a typical symptom. With some types, this is most likely upon waking up in the morning, after sitting at a desk, or after sitting in a car for a long time. With other types, stiffness may occur after exercise, or it may be persistent.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Difficulty moving a joint: If moving a joint or getting up from a chair is hard or painful, this could indicate arthritis or another joint problem.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-arthritis">Causes of arthritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-arthritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Possible causes may include:</p>
<ul>
<li>an injury, which can lead to degenerative arthritis</li>
<li>an abnormal metabolism, which can cause gout and calcium pyrophosphate deposition disease (CPPD)</li>
<li>a genetic inheritance, which can lead to developing osteoarthritis</li>
<li>an infection such as Lyme disease, which can trigger arthritis symptoms</li>
<li>an immune system dysfunction, such as the type that causes RA and lupus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-of-arthritis">Treatment of arthritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-arthritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medication</li>
<li>Medications will depend on the type of arthritis. Commonly used drugs include:</li>
<li>Analgesics: These reduce pain. However, they have no effect on inflammation. Examples include acetaminophen (Tylenol) and tramadol (Ultram).</li>
<li>Nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDs): These reduce both pain and inflammation. NSAIDs include available to purchase over-the-counter or online, including ibuprofen (Advil, Motrin IB) and naproxen sodium (Aleve). Some NSAIDs are available as creams, gels, or patches, which can be applied to specific joints.</li>
<li>Counterirritants: Some creams and ointments contain menthol or capsaicin, the ingredient that makes hot peppers spicy. Rubbing these on the skin over a painful joint can modulate pain signals from the joint and lessen pain.</li>
<li>Disease-modifying antirheumatic drugs (DMARDs): These are used to treat RA. DMARDs slow or stop the immune system from attacking the joints. Examples include methotrexate (Trexall) and hydroxychloroquine (Plaquenil).</li>
<li>Biologics: These are genetically engineered drugs that target various protein molecules involved in the immune response. Examples include etanercept (Enbrel) and infliximab (Remicade).</li>
<li>Corticosteroids: prednisone and cortisone reduce inflammation and suppress the immune system.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="natural-remedies">Natural remedies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#natural-remedies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A healthful, balanced diet, along with appropriate exercise and avoidance of smoking and drinking too much alcohol can help people with arthritis maintain their overall health and reduce symptom severity.</li>
<li>Diet</li>
<li>Eating some types of food may help reduce inflammation.</li>
<li>The following foods, found in a Mediterranean diet, can provide many nutrients that are good for joint health and can help relieve joint inflammation.</li>
<li>fish</li>
<li>nuts and seeds</li>
<li>fruits and vegetables</li>
<li>beans</li>
<li>olive oil</li>
<li>whole grains</li>
</ul>
<p>Physical therapy and exercise</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Doctors will often recommend a course of physical therapy to help patients with arthritis overcome some of the challenges and to reduce limitations on mobility.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Forms of physical therapy that may be recommended include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical therapy: specific exercises tailored to the condition and individual needs, sometimes combined with pain-relieving treatments such as ice or hot packs and massage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occupational therapy: practical advice on managing everyday tasks, choosing specialized aids and equipment, protecting the joints from further damage, and managing fatigue</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Surgery</p>
<ul>
<li>Depending on the type of arthritis a person has, different surgical treatments on the affected joints may be necessary. It may depend on the degree of a person’s symptoms and whether other treatments have been successful.</li>
</ul>
<p>Surgery options for arthritis include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>synovectomy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>total joint replacement (TJR)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>osteotomy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>joint fusion</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A bone tumor is a neoplastic growth of tissue in bone.</li>
<li>Abnormal growths found in the bone can be either benign (noncancerous) or malignant (cancerous)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Neoplasia : It is defined as a mass of tissue formed as result of abnormal, excessive, uncoordinated, autonomous and purposeless proliferation of cells.</li>
<li>Term Neoplasia includes both Benign and Malignant.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="differences-between-benign-and-malignant-tumors">Differences between benign and malignant tumors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differences-between-benign-and-malignant-tumors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Benign tumors</th><th>Malignant tumor</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Slowly growing mass</td><td>Rapidly growing mass</td></tr><tr><td>Regular surface, capsulated, not attached to deep structures</td><td>Irregular surfaces, Non-capsulated attached to deep structures</td></tr><tr><td>Noninvasive to another organ or tissues</td><td>Invasive to other organs</td></tr><tr><td>No spread or metastasis</td><td>Spread and metastasis</td></tr><tr><td>Well differentiated all the them</td><td>Poorly differentiated, moderately or well differentiated</td></tr><tr><td>No recurrence after surgery</td><td>Recurrence after surgery</td></tr><tr><td>No bleeding in cut surfaces</td><td>Bleeding from cut surfaces is common</td></tr><tr><td>Named by adding suffix –oma</td><td>Named by adding suffix sarcoma or carcinoma</td></tr><tr><td>Slight pressure effect on the neighboring organ</td><td>Remarkable pressure effect on neighboring tissue</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Metastasis-is the movement or spreading of cancer cells from one organ or tissue to another. Cancer cells usually spread through the blood or the lymph system. If a cancer spreads, it is said to have "metastasized."</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9918ba21.jpeg" alt="img-53.jpeg">
Benign Tumor</p>
<p>are not cancerous and spread.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-c9204ac3.jpeg" alt="img-54.jpeg">
Malignant Tumor</p>
<p>Cells are cancerous and can spread to other tissues and organs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetic disorders</li>
<li>Retinoblastoma</li>
<li>Paget disease</li>
<li>Radiation exposure</li>
<li>Bone marrow transplantation</li>
<li>Injuries</li>
</ul>
<p>Types of bone tumor</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Benign</th><th>Malignant</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Bone forming/Osteoblastic</td><td>Osteoma</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Osteoid Osteoma</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Osteoblastoma</td><td>Osteosarcoma</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Cartilage Forming</td><td>Enchondroma</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Osteocondroma</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Chondroblastoma</td><td>Chondrosarcoma</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Hematopoietic</td><td>—</td><td>Myeloma</td></tr><tr><td>Lymphoma</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Unknown</td><td>Giant Cell tumor</td><td>Malignant giant cell tumor</td></tr><tr><td>Ewing’s Sarcoma</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Notochordal</td><td>—</td><td>Chordoma</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">CLINICAL MANIFESTATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cardinal symptoms:</li>
<li>Pain, swelling and general discomfort</li>
<li>Limited mobility and spontaneous fracture may also be important feature.</li>
<li>Other symptoms:</li>
<li>Fever and night sweats</li>
<li>Painless mass or obvious bone growth</li>
<li>Varying degree of disability, weight loss, malaise.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>With spinal metastasis spinal cord compression may occur.</li>
<li>Neurologic deficit: e.g. Progressive pain, weakness, gait abnormality, paresthesia, paraplegia, urinary retention, loss of bowel and bladder control.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pain">pain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>first &amp; most common symptom.</li>
<li>may initially occur intermittently and only at rest</li>
<li>become more intense, disturb sleep at night, spread into the adjacent joint.</li>
<li>A further intensification of pain is experienced as a persistent and piercing pain.</li>
<li>becomes excruciating and intolerable, requiring opiate treatment.</li>
<li>In case of pressure on nerve trunks or nerve plexuses, the patient may experience radiating pain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="swelling">SWELLING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#swelling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>very long duration, especially in benign neoplasms &amp; cause no additional complaints.</li>
<li>In malignant tumours, swelling develops more rapidly.</li>
<li>may also cause skin changes, including tensed shining skin with prominent veins, livid colouring, hyperthermia, as well as striation of the skin and eventually, ulceration.</li>
<li>The mobility of the skin &amp; musculature above the tumour should also be assessed. The less the mobility, the more likely is this factor a criterion of malignancy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="limited-mobility">LIMITED MOBILITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#limited-mobility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mobility may be limited in cases of lesions close to the joint</li>
<li>In tumours such as osteoblastoma, chrondroblastoma, giant cell tumours and all types of sarcomas.</li>
<li>Occasionally it is not the tumour but reactive synovitis in the joint, especially in chondroblastoma, that causes limitation of movement and masks the true diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathological-fracture">PATHOLOGICAL FRACTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathological-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fracture is diagnosed early, as it causes the patient to seek attention immediately.</li>
<li>It may occur with no prior symptoms at all, as is frequently the case in juvenile cysts and in some non-ossifying bone.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e4b56578.jpeg" alt="img-55.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnosis">ASSESSMENT AND DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The differential diagnosis is based on history, physical examination and diagnostic studies.</li>
<li>Age: it is useful information before age of 5, a malignant tumor is often metastatic neuroblastoma; between 5 and 15 years old, osteosarcoma or Ewing sarcoma; and after 40 years, metastasis or myeloma.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-studies">Diagnostic studies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-studies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>X-rays: can show the location, size and shape of a bone tumor. Chest x-rays are performed to determine presence of lung metastasis.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b7be7a2f.jpeg" alt="img-56.jpeg">
X RAY BONE TUMORS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f286cbd7">Cont…<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f286cbd7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A Bone Scan: a test in which a small amount of radioactive material is injected into a blood vessel and travels through the bloodstream; it the collects in the bones and is directed by a scanner.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6f800bdf.jpeg" alt="img-57.jpeg">
BONE SCAN</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">Cont...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A Computed Tomography: a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, taken from different angles, that are created by a computer linked to an x-ray machine.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-18f514f6.jpeg" alt="img-58.jpeg"></p>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>A Magnetic resonance imaging: which uses a powerful magnet linked to a computer to create detailed pictures of areas inside the body without using x-rays.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-a51e8e08.jpeg" alt="img-59.jpeg">
MRI BONE TUMORS</p>
<p>Cont...</p>
<p>☐ Biopsy: removal of a tissue sample from the bone tumor.</p>
<ul>
<li>The biopsy is most conclusive test because it confirms tumor is malignant or benign and confirms the cancer stage.</li>
</ul>
<p>☐ Two type of biopsy done based on tumor size and type:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Needle biopsy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Incisional biopsy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An incisional biopsy is when a small cut (incision) is made into an area of abnormal tissue and a small piece of it is removed from the body. The piece of tissue that has been removed (biopsy sample) is then sent off to the laboratory for analysis.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="incisional-biopsy">Incisional biopsy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incisional-biopsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-aba3d52d.jpeg" alt="img-60.jpeg"></p>
<p>Partial removal of skin tissue</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b576aa82.jpeg" alt="img-61.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A needle biopsy is a procedure to obtain a sample of cells from your body for laboratory testing. Common needle biopsy procedures include fine-needle aspiration and core needle biopsy. Needle biopsy may be used to take tissue or fluid samples from muscles, bones, and other organs, such as the liver or lungs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fine-needle aspiration. This type of needle biopsy uses a thin, hollow needle to draw cells from your body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Core needle biopsy. This type of needle biopsy uses a wider needle than does fine-needle aspiration. The needle used during a core needle biopsy is a hollow tube that allows the doctor to extract a sample of tissue for testing.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6ceb1c21.jpeg" alt="img-62.jpeg"></p>
<p>Cont...</p>
<p>☐ Blood test:</p>
<ul>
<li>Alkaline phosphate</li>
<li>Biochemical assay of blood and urine: Elevated serum ALP</li>
<li>Calcium levels: Hypercalcemia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Chemotherapy</li>
<li>Radiation therapy</li>
<li>Surgical management</li>
<li>Targeted therapy</li>
<li>Other treatments</li>
<li>Nursing management</li>
</ul>
