<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemotherapy">chemotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Use of anticancer drugs to kill cancer cells. Usually received in combination.</li>
<li>Most commonly used drugs:</li>
<li>Doxorubicin (40-60 mg/m2)</li>
<li>Cisplatin (75-100 mg/m2)</li>
<li>Carboplatin</li>
<li>Ifosfamide (1.2 g/m2)</li>
<li>Cyclophosphamide (10-15mg/kg iv; 1-5 mg/kg oral)</li>
<li>Methotrexate (oral/iv)</li>
<li>Vincristine (1.4mg/m2)</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-d67eb3b8.jpeg" alt="img-63.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-chemotherapy">Side effects of chemotherapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-chemotherapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Some common temporary side effects can include nausea and vomiting, loss of appetite, hair loss, mouth sores.</li>
<li>Ifosfamide and cyclophosphamide can cause hemorrhagic cystitis &amp; can be prevented by giving a drug called mesna along with the chemo.</li>
<li>Cisplatin may cause neuropathy leading to problems with numbness, tingling, and even pain in the hands and feet. Nephropathy can also occur after treatment with cisplatin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="radiation-therapy">Radiation therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiation-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involves use of high energy x-rays to kill tumor cells</li>
<li>May be used in combination with surgery</li>
<li>Often used if chemotherapy cannot treat the tumor such as chondrosarcoma.</li>
<li>May be used in patients those refuse surgery to reduce pain and decrease the chance of bone fracture</li>
<li>Side effects: fatigue, loss of appetite, skin changes ranging from redness, hair loss, blistering and peeling may occur due to radiation therapy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-management">Surgical management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Removal of entire tumor with negative margins</li>
<li>Special surgical techniques may be used to minimize the amount of healthy tissue removed with tumor.</li>
<li>It ranges from local excision to amputation and disarticulation.</li>
<li>May include limb salvage and reconstructive surgery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="amputation">amputation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amputation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>surgery to remove part or all of a limb.</li>
<li>amputation removes the limb part with the tumor, some healthy tissue above it, and everything below it.</li>
<li>In the past, amputation was the main way to treat bone cancers found in the arms or legs.</li>
<li>For example, an amputation may be needed if removing all of the cancer requires removing essential nerves, arteries, or muscles that would leave the limb without good function.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Acute Pain r/t disease process (compression/destruction of nerve tissue, infiltration of nerves or their vascular supply, obstruction of a nerve pathway, inflammation)</li>
<li>Altered Nutrition: Less Than Body Requirements r/t consequences of chemotherapy, radiation, surgery, e.g., anorexia, gastric irritation, taste distortions, nausea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f286cbd7">Cont…<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f286cbd7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fatigue r/t altered body chemistry: side effects of pain &amp; other medications, chemotherapy</li>
<li>Risk for Infection r/t immunosuppression</li>
<li>Risk for Fluid Volume Deficit r/t excessive losses (vomiting, diarrhea) or impaired intake.</li>
<li>Risk for Altered Oral Mucous Membranes r/t Side effect of some chemotherapeutic agents</li>
<li>Risk for Impaired Skin Integrity r/t effects of radiation and chemotherapy</li>
<li>Situational Low Self-Esteem r/t feelings of lack of control and doubt regarding acceptance by others</li>
<li>Fear/Anxiety r/t threat of death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-pain">Acute pain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>pain history (location, frequency, duration &amp; intensity (0–10 scale), or verbal rating scale &amp; relief measures used.</li>
<li>Evaluate and be aware of painful effects of particular therapies</li>
<li>Provide nonpharmacological comfort measures (massage, repositioning, backrub) and diversional activities (music, television)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f286cbd7">Cont…<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f286cbd7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>use of <strong>stress</strong> management skills or complementary therapies (relaxation techniques, visualization, guided imagery, biofeedback, laughter, music, aromatherapy, and therapeutic touch).</li>
<li>cutaneous stimulation (heat or cold, massage).</li>
<li>Evaluate pain relief and control at regular intervals.</li>
<li>Inform patient of the expected therapeutic effects and discuss management of side effects</li>
<li>Discuss use of additional alternative or complementary therapies (acupuncture and acupressure).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diosturbed-nutrition-less-than-body-requirements">Diosturbed nutrition: less than body requirements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diosturbed-nutrition-less-than-body-requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor daily food intake; have patient keep food diary as indicated.</li>
<li>Measure height, weight or other anthropometric measurements as appropriate. Weigh daily or as indicated.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to eat high-calorie, nutrient-rich diet, with adequate fluid intake. Encourage use of supplements and frequent or smaller meals spaced throughout the day.</li>
<li>Create pleasant dining atmosphere; encourage patient to share meals with family and friends.</li>
</ul>
<p>cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Control environmental factors (strong or noxious odors or noise). Avoid overly sweet, fatty, or spicy foods.</li>
<li>Encourage use of relaxation techniques, visualization, guided imagery, moderate exercise before meals.</li>
<li>Administer antiemetic as appropriate.</li>
<li>Insert and maintain NG or feeding tube for enteric feedings, or central line for total parenteral nutrition (TPN) if indicated.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2cb76e9d.jpeg" alt="img-64.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fatigue">fatigue<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fatigue" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Have patient rate fatigue, using a numeric scale, if possible, and the time of day when it is most severe.</li>
<li>Plan care to allow for rest periods. Schedule activities for periods when patient has most energy. Involve patient in schedule planning.</li>
<li>Establish realistic activity goals with patient.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Assist with self-care needs when indicated; keep bed in low position, pathways clear of furniture; assist with ambulation.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to do whatever possible (self-bathing, sitting up in chair, walking). Increase activity level as individual is able.</li>
<li>Monitor physiological response to activity (changes in BP, heart and respiratory rate).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-of-infection">Risk of infection<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-of-infection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Promote good handwashing procedures by staff and visitors. Screen and limit visitors who may have infections.</li>
<li>Emphasize personal hygiene.</li>
<li>Monitor temperature.</li>
<li>Assess all systems (skin, respiratory, genitourinary) for signs and symptoms of infection on a continual basis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Promote adequate rest and exercise periods.</li>
<li>Stress importance of good oral hygiene.</li>
<li>Avoid or limit invasive procedures. Adhere to aseptic techniques.</li>
<li>Monitor CBC with differential WBC and granulocyte count, and <strong>platelets</strong> as indicated.</li>
<li>Obtain cultures as indicated.</li>
<li>Administer <strong>antibiotics</strong> as indicated.</li>
</ul>
<p>Risk for fluid volume deficit:</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor I&amp;O and specific gravity; include all output sources, (emesis, diarrhea, draining wounds. Calculate 24-hr balance).</li>
<li>Weigh as indicated.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs. Evaluate peripheral pulses, capillary refill.</li>
<li>Assess skin turgor and moisture of mucous membranes. Note reports of thirst.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Encourage increased fluid intake to 3000 mL per day as individually appropriate or tolerated.</li>
<li>Observe for <strong>bleeding</strong> tendencies (oozing from mucous membranes, puncture sites); presence of ecchymosis or petechiae.</li>
<li>Avoid trauma and apply pressure to puncture sites.</li>
<li>Provide IV fluids as indicated.</li>
<li>Monitor laboratory studies (CBC, <strong>electrolytes</strong>, serum albumin).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-for-altered-oral-mucous-membranes">Risk for altered oral mucous membranes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-for-altered-oral-mucous-membranes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Assess dental health and oral hygiene periodically.</li>
<li>Use of mouthwash made from warm saline, dilute solution of hydrogen peroxide or baking soda and water</li>
<li>Brush with soft toothbrush</li>
<li>Floss gently</li>
<li>Keep lips moist</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Encourage use of mints or hard candy or artificial saliva as indicated.</li>
<li>Instruct regarding dietary changes: avoid hot or spicy foods,</li>
<li>Encourage fluid intake as individually tolerated.</li>
<li>Discuss limitation of smoking and alcohol intake.</li>
<li>Monitor for and explain to patient signs of oral superinfection (thrush).</li>
<li>Culture suspicious oral lesions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-for-impaired-skin-integrity">Risk for impaired skin integrity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-for-impaired-skin-integrity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Assess skin frequently for side effects of cancer therapy; note breakdown and delayed wound healing.</li>
<li>Bathe with lukewarm water and mild soap.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to avoid vigorous rubbing and scratching and to pat skin dry instead of rubbing.</li>
<li>Turn or reposition frequently.</li>
<li>Review skin care protocol for patient receiving radiation therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Avoid applying heat or attempting to wash off marks or tattoos</li>
<li>Recommend wearing soft, loose cotton clothing; Encourage liberal use of sunscreen &amp; protective clothing.</li>
<li>Assess skin, IV site, vein for erythema, edema, tenderness, itching and burning; swelling, soreness; blisters progressing to ulceration or tissue necrosis.</li>
<li>Wash skin immediately with soap and water if <strong>antineoplastic agents</strong> are spilled on unprotected skin (patient or caregiver).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="situational-low-self-esteem">Situational low self-esteem<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#situational-low-self-esteem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Discuss with patient how the diagnosis and treatment are affecting the patient's personal life, home and work activities.</li>
<li>Review anticipated side effects associated with a particular treatment, including possible effects on sexual activity and sense of attractiveness and desirability (alopecia, disfiguring surgery). Tell patient that not all side effects occur, and others may be minimized or controlled.</li>
</ul>
<p>Cont...</p>
<ul>
<li>Encourage discussion of concerns about effects of cancer and treatments on role as homemaker, wage earner, parent, and so forth.</li>
<li>Evaluate support structures available to and used by patient.</li>
<li>Provide emotional support for patient during diagnostic tests and treatment phase.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fear-anxiety">Fear/anxiety<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fear-anxiety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Review patient's previous experience with cancer.</li>
<li>Encourage patient to share thoughts and feelings.</li>
<li>Provide open environment in which patient feels safe to discuss feelings</li>
<li>Maintain frequent contact with patient.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f286cbd7">Cont…<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f286cbd7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Explain the recommended treatment, its purpose, and potential side effects. Help patient prepare for treatments.</li>
<li>Explain procedures, providing opportunity for questions and honest answers. Stay with patient during anxiety-producing procedures and consultations.</li>
<li>Promote calm, quiet environment.</li>
<li>Encourage and foster patient interaction with support systems</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="deformities">DEFORMITIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#deformities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="scoliosis">Scoliosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scoliosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Scoliosis is a side-to-side (lateral) curvature of the spine of 10 degrees or greater</li>
<li>Viewed from the rear, the spine usually appears to form a straight vertical line. In scoliosis there is a lateral (side-to-side) curve in the spine usually combined with a rotation of the vertebrae. A small degree of lateral curvature does not cause any medical problems but larger curves can cause postural imbalance and lead to muscle fatigue and pain. In more severe scoliosis breathing is impaired and can lead to spondylosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="scoliosis-causes">Scoliosis (causes)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scoliosis-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Idiopathic</li>
<li>Congenital scoliosis is due to congenital birth defects in the spine, often associated with other structural defects.</li>
<li>Neuromuscular scoliosis is due to loss of control of the nerves or muscles which support the spine. The most common causes of this type of scoliosis are cerebral palsy and muscular dystrophy.</li>
<li>Degenerative scoliosis may be caused by degeneration of the discs which separate the vertebrae or arthritis in the joints that link them.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-f6771ae0.jpeg" alt="img-65.jpeg">
Spine</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-90d3c32e.jpeg" alt="img-66.jpeg">
Figure 66-3 A normal spine and three abnormalities. (A) Kyphosis: an increased convexity or roundness of the spine's thoracic curve. (B) Lordosis: swayback; exaggeration of the lumbar spine curve. (C) Scoliosis: a lateral curvature of the spine.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-328c9d9a.jpeg" alt="img-67.jpeg"></p>
<p>Copyright © 2004 Lippincott Williams &amp; Wilkins.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>X-ray: Application of radiation to produce a film or picture of a part of the body can show the structure of the vertebrae and the outline of the joints. X-rays of the spine are obtained to search for other potential causes of pain, i.e. infections, fractures, deformities, etc.</li>
<li>Computed tomography scan (CT or CAT scan): A diagnostic image created after a computer reads X-rays; can show the shape and size of the spinal canal, its contents and the structures around it. Very good at visualizing bony structures.</li>
<li>Magnetic resonance imaging (MRI): A diagnostic test that produces three-dimensional images of body structures using powerful magnets and computer technology; can show the spinal cord, nerve roots and surrounding areas, as well as enlargement, degeneration and deformities.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment</p>
<p>-When there is a confirmed diagnosis of scoliosis, there are several issues to assess that can help determine treatment options:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Spinal maturity – is the patient's spine still growing and changing?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Degree and extent of curvature – how severe is the curve and how does it affect the patient's lifestyle?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Location of curve – according to some experts, thoracic curves are more likely to progress than curves in other regions of the spine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Possibility of curve progression – patients who have large curves prior to their adolescent growth spurts are more likely to experience curve progression.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Observation</li>
<li>Bracing</li>
<li>Surgery</li>
</ul>
<p>Observation</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In many children with scoliosis, the spinal curve is mild enough to not require treatment. However, if the doctor is worried that the curve may be increasing, he or she may wish to examine the child every four to six months throughout adolescence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In adults with scoliosis, X-rays are usually recommended once every five years, unless symptoms are getting progressively worse.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bracing</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Braces are only effective in patients who have not reached skeletal maturity. If the child is still growing and his or her curve is between 25 degrees and 40 degrees, a brace may be recommended to prevent the curve from progressing. There have been improvements in brace design and the newer models fit under the arm, not around the neck.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There are several different types of braces available. While there is some disagreement among experts as to which type of brace is most effective, large studies indicate that braces, when used with full compliance, successfully stop curve progression in about 80 percent of children with scoliosis. For optimal effectiveness, the brace should be checked regularly to assure a proper fit and may need to be worn 16 to 23 hours every day until growth stops.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="braces">BRACES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#braces" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="boston-brace">Boston Brace<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#boston-brace" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="milwaukee-brace">Milwaukee Brace<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#milwaukee-brace" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinecor-brace">SpineCor Brace<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinecor-brace" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2e3d2e58.jpeg" alt="img-70.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cheneau-brace">Cheneau Brace<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cheneau-brace" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2d3a24ff.jpeg" alt="img-71.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-best-treatment-is-exercise">THE BEST TREATMENT IS EXERCISE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-best-treatment-is-exercise" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>To provide rapid pain relief and functional improvement</li>
<li>To create a lifestyle habit for continued improvement and stability</li>
<li>To prevent age and hormone-related declines in bone density and strength</li>
<li>To stabilize scoliotic curve</li>
<li>Improve fitness, muscle strength and power.</li>
<li>Improve proprioception</li>
<li>Improve range of motion</li>
<li>Improve tolerance for prolonged activities</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e4d9ca52.jpeg" alt="img-72.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-best-treatment-is-exercise">THE BEST TREATMENT IS EXERCISE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-best-treatment-is-exercise" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-exercises-for-scoliosis">Types of exercises for scoliosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-exercises-for-scoliosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Symmetrical exercises</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Goals – To strengthen back and abdominal muscles and for functional improvement in ranges of joint motion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breathing exercises</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Goals – To increase lung volume and thorax mobility and flexibility.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Asymmetrical exercises</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Goals – For lengthening muscles on the shortened side, and for contracting muscles on the lengthened side.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Static exercises body weight (hanging or traction exercises)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Goals – For releasing tension along the spine</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-8ba00dc0.jpeg" alt="img-73.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-83ae6837.jpeg" alt="img-74.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">DEFINITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Kyphosis is a spinal disorder in which an excessive outward curve of the spine results in an abnormal rounding of the upper back. The condition is sometimes known as "roundback" or—in the case of a severe curve—as "hunchback."</li>
<li>Kyphosis can occur at any age, but is common during adolescence.</li>
<li>Normal kyphosis angles vary between 20° and 40° in the younger public</li>
<li>48° to 50° in women and about 44° in men in older populations.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-47a98451.jpeg" alt="img-75.jpeg">
SHARE PERCENT OF MEDICAL DISORDER AND RESEARCH. ALL RIGHTS RESERVED.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-kyphosis">TYPES OF KYPHOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>POSTURAL KYPHOSIS</li>
<li>SCHEUERMANN'S KYPHOSIS</li>
<li>CONGENITAL KYPHOSIS</li>
<li>NUTRITIONAL KYPHOSIS</li>
<li>GIBBUS DEFORMITY</li>
<li>POST-TRAUMATIC KYPHOSIS</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5fd7573f.jpeg" alt="img-76.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postural-kyphosis">POSTURAL KYPHOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postural-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is the most common type of kyphosis.</li>
<li>More common in girls than in boys which is typically noticed in adolescent age.</li>
<li>It is caused by poor posture and weakening of the muscles, ligaments in the back. (paraspinal muscles).</li>
<li>The vertebrae are typically placed in postural kyphosis.</li>
<li>It progressively gets worse with time.</li>
<li>SYMPTOMS: Pain and muscle spasm.</li>
<li>In young age it is called slouching and in old age it is called “Dowager’s hump”.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9cba1cbb.jpeg" alt="img-77.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="scheuermann-kyphosis">SCHEUERMANN KYPHOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scheuermann-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3edf969b.jpeg" alt="img-78.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>It is significantly worse cosmetically and can cause varying degrees of pain, and can also affect different areas of the spine (the most common being the mid-thoracic area).</li>
<li>Scheuermann's kyphosis is considered a form of juvenile osteochondrosis of the spine, and is more commonly called Scheuermann's disease.</li>
<li>It is found mostly in teenagers and presents a significantly worse deformity than postural kyphosis.</li>
<li>A patient suffering from Scheuermann's kyphosis cannot consciously correct posture.</li>
<li>The apex of the curve, located in the thoracic vertebrae, is quite rigid. The patient may feel pain at this apex, which can be aggravated by physical activity and by long periods of standing or sitting.</li>
</ul>
<p>This can have a significantly detrimental effect on their lives, as their level of activity is curbed by their condition; they may feel isolated or uneasy amongst peers if they are children, depending on the level of deformity.</p>
<p>Whereas in postural kyphosis, the vertebrae and discs appear normal, in Scheuermann's kyphosis, they are irregular, often herniated, and wedge-shaped over at least three adjacent levels.</p>
<p>Fatigue is a very common symptom, most likely because of the intense muscle work that has to be put into standing or sitting properly. The condition appears to run in families. Most patients who undergo surgery to correct their kyphosis have Scheuermann's disease.</p>
<p>BRACEABILITY</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postural-kyphosis">Postural Kyphosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postural-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Excessive curve of the back sounds when bending</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="scheuermann-s-kyphosis">Scheuermann's Kyphosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scheuermann-s-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>No smoothing of the back occurs when bending due to structural changes in the spine</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-fbec705d.jpeg" alt="img-79.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e9c854d3.jpeg" alt="img-80.jpeg"></p>
<p>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutritional-kyphosis">NUTRITIONAL KYPHOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutritional-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Can result from nutritional deficiencies, especially during childhood, such as vitamin D deficiency (producing rickets and osteomalacia in adults), which softens bones and results in curving of the spine and limbs under the child's body weight.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-43c9d654.jpeg" alt="img-81.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiology">ETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Aging, especially if you have poor posture</li>
<li>Muscle weakness in the upper back</li>
<li>Scheuermann’s disease, which occurs in children and has no known cause</li>
<li>Arthritis or other bone degeneration diseases</li>
<li>Osteoporosis, or the loss of bone strength due to age</li>
<li>Injury to the spine</li>
<li>Slipped discs</li>
<li>Scoliosis, or spinal curvature</li>
<li>Infection in the spine</li>
<li>Birth defects, such as spina bifida</li>
<li>Tumours</li>
<li>Diseases of the connective tissues</li>
<li>Polio</li>
<li>Paget disease</li>
<li>Muscular dystrophy</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-18597f9e.jpeg" alt="img-82.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-symptoms-of-kyphosis">COMMON SYMPTOMS OF KYPHOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-symptoms-of-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Visible hump on back</li>
<li>Spine stiffness</li>
<li>Rounded shoulder</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Mild back pain</li>
<li>Tight hamstrings (muscles in the back of the thigh)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="serious-symptoms">SERIOUS SYMPTOMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#serious-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Numbness, weakness, or tingling in the legs</li>
<li>Loss of sensation</li>
<li>Shortness of breath</li>
<li>Breathing difficulties.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-29631d14.jpeg" alt="img-83.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnosis-of-kyphosis">Diagnosis of Kyphosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-kyphosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Neurological examination of the patient</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e0301abd.jpeg" alt="img-84.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-treatment">MEDICAL TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Medications:</li>
<li>Non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drugs such as:</li>
<li>Advil and Motrin (ibuprofen)</li>
<li>Aleve (naproxen) can help relieve back pain.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-1e9b1a1d.jpeg" alt="img-85.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-surgical-treatment">NON-SURGICAL TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-surgical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Braces. Braces may be recommended for younger patients with Scheuermann’s kyphosis who are still growing.</li>
<li>The severity of the curve will determine the type of brace and amount of time it needs to be worn. Typically, the brace is worn until the child reaches skeletal maturity (when growing is complete).</li>
<li>The Milwaukee brace is one particular body brace that is often used to treat kyphosis in the US.</li>
<li>Modern CAD/CAM braces are used in Europe to treat different types of kyphosis. These are much easier to wear and have better in-brace corrections than reported for the Milwaukee brace.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9909006e.jpeg" alt="img-86.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-treatment">SURGICAL TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are multiple surgical procedures that can be applied, depending on:</li>
<li>Flexibility: X-rays will be taken to determine how flexible the spine is. If it's flexible, a posterior approach may be adequate. If the patient is less flexible, an anterior or combined approach will be needed. These techniques are based on bone fusion with screws and rods.</li>
<li>Osteotomy (a surgical operation in which a bone is cut to shorten, lengthen, or change its alignment.).</li>
<li>°</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-61cd9028.jpeg" alt="img-87.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-699ce42a.jpeg" alt="img-88.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Osteoporosis: An osteoporotic kyphosis can be caused by a collapsed vertebra.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This can be treated with a kyphoplasty, whereby a balloon is inserted into the affected vertebra and filled with liquid that hardens to restore the vertebral height.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vertebroplasty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They even have resulted in a decreased kyphosis angle. reduced pain, improved physical function, vertebral height restoration of up to 90%, and kyphosis angle correction ranging from 8.5° to 14</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-277c51b0.jpeg" alt="img-89.jpeg">
Balloon inserted into fractured vertebra</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3158ee2b.jpeg" alt="img-90.jpeg">
Balloon inflated inside damaged vertebra</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-816ce4a6.jpeg" alt="img-91.jpeg">
Special material injected into fractured vertebra</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e3fb09a6.jpeg" alt="img-92.jpeg">
Special material hardens, stabilizing vertebra</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physiotherapy-treatment">PHYSIOTHERAPY TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiotherapy-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It most commonly occurs in thoracic spine:</p>
<ul>
<li>Thoracic joint mobilizations are required in patients diagnosed with hyperkyphosis because of the reduced thoracic motion. e.g. Scapular, myofascial and spinal mobilization techniques increase postural alignment.</li>
<li>Self-mobilization techniques: Diaphragmatic breathing on foam roller for expanding the rib cage.</li>
</ul>
<p>Pursed lip breathing exercises.</p>
<ul>
<li>Teach these exercises at home.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-01776130.jpeg" alt="img-93.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-332d4c2e.jpeg" alt="img-94.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Stretching: To decrease tonus in the muscles:</li>
<li>Chest stretching on foam roller: lengthening pectoralis muscles</li>
<li>Prone hip extension/ knee flexion: lengthening iliopsoas and rectus femoris</li>
<li>Supine knee extension with hip at 90° flexion: lengthening hamstrings.</li>
<li>Pain management using modalities such as</li>
<li>Hot packs</li>
<li>Cryotherapy</li>
<li>Electrical stimulation such as transcutaneous electrical nerve stimulation (TENS).</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-8131a1bf.jpeg" alt="img-95.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-21c6eba1.jpeg" alt="img-96.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prognosis">PROGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Scheuermann kyphosis disorder in adolescents stop once their growth stops.</li>
<li>If the disorder occurs due to degenerative types, then they may need a surgical correction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Decreased lung capacity</li>
<li>Disability pain</li>
<li>Neurological symptoms including weakness in legs or paralysis.</li>
<li>Round back deformity.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-fcc40966.jpeg" alt="img-97.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-3bc45747.jpeg" alt="img-98.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lordosis">LORDOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lordosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A normal spine when viewed from behind appears straight.</li>
<li>Lordosis is a medical term used to describe an inward curvature of a portion of the lumbar and cervical vertebral column.</li>
</ul>
<p>Lordosis</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-17ad15a4.jpeg" alt="img-99.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prominence of buttocks.</li>
<li>Back pain.</li>
<li>Pain down the legs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Common causes of lordosis</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Lordosis can affect people of any age. Certain conditions and factors can increase your risk for lordosis. This includes:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spondylolisthesis: Spondylolisthesis is a spinal condition in which one of the lower vertebras slips forward onto the bone below. It’s usually treated with therapy or surgery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Achondroplasia: Achondroplasia is one of the most common types of dwarfism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Osteoporosis: Osteoporosis is a bone disease that causes a loss of bone density, which increases your risk of fractures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Osteosarcoma: Osteosarcoma is a bone cancer that typically develops in the shinbone near the knee, the thighbone near the knee, or the upper arm bone near the shoulder.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obesity: Obesity is an epidemic in the U.S. This condition puts people at a higher risk for serious diseases, such as type 2 diabetes, heart disease, and cancer. .</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-evaluation">Diagnostic Evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>X-rays: done to measure and evaluate curve.</li>
<li>Bone scans: to evaluate degenerative or arthritic changes. Also helps to find out bone tumors.</li>
<li>MRI: to rule out associated problems.</li>
<li>CT scan.</li>
<li>Blood investigations.</li>
<li>Early detection of Lordosis is important for proper and successful treatment.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b517127b.jpeg" alt="img-100.jpeg">
Normal spine</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-161b60c2.jpeg" alt="img-101.jpeg">
Lordosis of the spine
Exaggerated lumbar curve</p>
<p>How to treat lordosis</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Most people with lordosis don’t require medical treatment unless it’s a severe case. Treatment for lordosis will depend on how severe your curve is and the presence of other symptoms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treatment options include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>medication, to reduce pain and swelling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>daily physical therapy, to strengthen muscles and range of motion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>weight loss, to help posture</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>braces, in children and teens</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>surgery, in severe cases with neurological concerns</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>nutritional supplements such as vitamin D</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="congenital">Congenital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Talipes</li>
<li>Osteogenetic imperfecta</li>
<li>Hip dysplasia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="congenital-talipes">Congenital Talipes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-talipes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Talipes Equinovarus is a congenital disorder in which an infant is born with one foot or both feet deformed into the shape of a club</li>
<li>The bones, muscles, and other connective tissues are usually present though deformed in structure</li>
<li>Associated with factors such as factors the fetus's position in the uterus and genetic factors</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-bf245fec.jpeg" alt="img-102.jpeg">
Talipes cavus</p>
