<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="colchicine-colcrys">Colchicine (Colcrys)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#colchicine-colcrys" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Comes in a tablet to take by mouth.</li>
<li>Side effect: Mild nausea, stomach pain and mild diarrhea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="allopurinol">Allopurinol<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#allopurinol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Comes as a tablet to take by mouth, take it around the same time every day</li>
<li>Side effect: Upset stomach, diarrhea and drowsiness</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-2a557538.jpeg" alt="img-166.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-treatment-con-t">Medical Treatment con't<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-treatment-con-t" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-414f8789.jpeg" alt="img-167.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="probenecid">Probenecid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#probenecid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Comes in a tablet to take by mouth. (taken two times a day)</li>
<li>Side effect: Headache, Vomiting, Loss of appetite and Dizziness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="corticosteroid-prednisone">Corticosteroid (Prednisone)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corticosteroid-prednisone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Comes in a tablet to take by mouth.</li>
<li>Side effect: Fluid retention, Increase BP, Mood Swings</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-0f806580.jpeg" alt="img-168.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-treatment">Surgical Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If gout symptom have occurred off and on without treatment, uric acid crystals may have built up in the joints to form gritty, chalky nodules called <strong>tophi</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e72d661c.jpeg" alt="img-169.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-treatment-con-t">Surgical Treatment con't<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-treatment-con-t" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This tophi can cause infection pain, pressure, and deformed joints.</p>
<p>Surgery will recommend by do the excision to remove the tophi</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-83807634.jpeg" alt="img-170.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-5ea2b053.jpeg" alt="img-171.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-plan">NURSING CARE PLAN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing Diagnosis: Acute pain related to swelling joints</p>
<p>Goal: Pain will be relieved</p>
<p>Nursing Intervention:</p>
<ul>
<li>The pain should be assessed on an ongoing basis using a scale of one to 10 to describe the severity.</li>
<li>Use cognitive therapy such as creative visualization to distract the patient from his pain.</li>
<li>Apply cold packs to inflamed joints to ease discomfort and reduce swelling.</li>
<li>Encourage the patient to perform techniques that promote rest and relaxation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-plan-con-t">NURSING CARE PLAN con't<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-plan-con-t" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing Diagnosis: Activity Intolerance related to pain</p>
<p>Goal: Patient can do the activity daily living (ADL)</p>
<p>Nursing Intervention:</p>
<ul>
<li>Evaluate or continuously monitor degree of joint inflammation or pain.</li>
<li>Assess the level of intolerance and assist the patient in activities she feels unable to perform.</li>
<li>Assist with activity passive range of motion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-plan-con-t">NURSING CARE PLAN con't<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-plan-con-t" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nursing Diagnosis: Hyperthermia related to inflammatory process</p>
<p>Goal: Client will be maintain normal body temperature without complication</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-intervention">Nursing Intervention:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-intervention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor vital sign</li>
<li>Provide tepid sponge bath (if not contraindicated)</li>
<li>Promote client safety.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-presentation">CLINICAL PRESENTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Back pain relieved by movement</li>
<li>Difficulty in bending</li>
<li>Straightening of normal curvature of spine</li>
<li>Loss of appetite</li>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Sensitivity to light</li>
<li>Difficulty in taking breath</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Exercise
Regular daily exercises can help create better posture and flexibility as well as help lessen pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Posture
Practicing good posture techniques will also help avoid some of the complications of AS including stiffness and flexion deformities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Heat/Cold
Applying heat to stiff joints and tight muscles can help reduce pain and soreness. Applying cold to inflamed areas can help reduce swelling. Hot baths and showers can also help provide relief.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Drugs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nonsteroidal anti-inflammatory drugs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surgery</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In severe cases surgery can be an option in the form of joint replacements, particularly in the knees and hips. Surgical correction is also possible for those with severe flexion deformities</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Others</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Massage and using electrical stimulators for pain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maintaining a healthy body weight</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Balanced diet</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnosis">Nursing Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Activity intolerance related to pain and inflammation of joints</li>
<li>Chronic pain related to deteriorating bone and cartilage of joints</li>
<li>Deficient diversional activity related to pain, stiffness, and limitation of joint motion</li>
<li>Disturbed sensory perception (visual) related to eye inflammation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rheumatoid-arthritis">RHEUMATOID ARTHRITIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rheumatoid-arthritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Rheumatoid arthritis (RA) is a chronic autoimmune disease.</li>
<li>It causes joints to swell and can result in pain, stiffness, and progressive loss of function.</li>
<li>RA often affects pairs of joints (both hands, both feet, etc) and can affect more than one joint, including the small joints in the wrists and hands.</li>
<li>Over time, other joints can be affected such as shoulders, elbows, knees, feet, and ankles.</li>
</ul>
<p>Jegan</p>
<ul>
<li>Over time, the inflammation of RA can cause damage to the joints.</li>
<li>In some patients, this may lead to permanent joint damage.</li>
<li>As this joint damage progresses, in severe cases, it can cause deformity of the joints and loss of function.</li>
<li>It may begin to interfere with daily activities, making them more difficult and painful to do</li>
<li>RA often begins in middle age, but can start at any age.</li>
<li>RA affects 2 to 3 times as many women than men.</li>
</ul>
<p>Jegan</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ce748c07.jpeg" alt="img-185.jpeg">
Healthy Joint</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-dcd5a9e0.jpeg" alt="img-186.jpeg">
Rheumatoid Arthritis</p>
<ul>
<li>First, the Antigen Presenting Cell usually a macrophage in synovium engulfs the antigen.</li>
<li>Enzymes (peroxides) inside the APC break down the antigen into smaller particles</li>
<li>The processed antigens are transported to the surface of the APC</li>
<li>Antigen is now presented to T-cells (CD4 cells ie. T-helper cell) or CD8 (cytotoxic T cells) which the T-cell receptor (TCR) recognizes and binds to.</li>
</ul>
<p>vegan</p>
<p>Jegan</p>
<p>Once the T-cell binds to the Antigen it becomes activated, the APC then secrete cytokines like</p>
<ul>
<li>Interleukin-1 (IL-1)</li>
<li>Interferon-alpha (IFN-α)</li>
<li>Interferon-gamma (IFN-γ)</li>
<li>Tumor necrosis factor (TNF)</li>
</ul>
<p>APC also Secretes Lysozymes, Elastases and Collagenases these enzymes cause cartilage breakdown.</p>
<ul>
<li>On exposure to IL-1, synoviocytes proliferate and produce following factors</li>
<li>Interleukin-6 (IL-6)</li>
<li>Prostaglandin's (e.g., PGE2), and platelet-activating factor, which are involved in the pain mechanism.</li>
<li>Matrix Metalloproteases that cause activation of collagenase, an enzyme required for cartilage breakdown.</li>
</ul>
<p>Jegan</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms">SYMPTOMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Joint pain</li>
<li>Joint tenderness</li>
<li>Joint swelling</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-and-rehabilitation">MANAGEMENT AND REHABILITATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-and-rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>PRINCIPLES OF REHABILITATION</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A: Avoid aggravation. It is important not to aggravate the injury during the rehabilitation process. Therapeutic exercise, if administered incorrectly or without good judgment, has the potential to exacerbate the injury, that is, make it worse. The primary concern of the therapeutic exercise program is to advance the injured individual gradually and steadily and to keep setbacks to a minimum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>T: Timing. The therapeutic exercise portion of the rehabilitation program should begin as soon as possible—that is, as soon as it can occur without causing aggravation. The sooner patients can begin the exercise portion of the rehabilitation program, the sooner they can return to full activity. Following injury, rest is sometimes necessary, but too much rest can actually be detrimental to recovery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>C: Compliance. Without a compliant patient, the rehabilitation program will not be successful. To ensure compliance, it is important to inform the patient of the content of the program and the expected course of rehabilitation. Patients are more compliant when they are better aware of the program they will be following, the work they will have to do, and the components of the rehabilitation process.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>I: Individualization. Each person responds differently to an injury and to the subsequent rehabilitation program. Expecting a patient to progress in the same way as the last patient you had with a similar injury will be frustrating for both you and the patient. It is first necessary to recognize that each person is different. It is also important to realize that even though an injury may seem the same in type and severity as another, undetectable differences can change an individual's response to it. Individual physiological and chemical differences profoundly affect a patient's specific responses to an injury.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>S: Specific sequencing. A therapeutic exercise program should follow a specific sequence of events. This specific sequence is determined by the body's physiological healing response and is briefly addressed in the next section of this chapter.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>I: Intensity. The intensity level of the therapeutic exercise program must challenge the patient and the injured area but at the same time must not cause aggravation. Knowing when to increase intensity without overtaxing the injury requires observation of the patient's response and consideration of the healing process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>T: Total patient. You must consider the total patient in the rehabilitation process. It is important for the unaffected areas of the body to stay finely tuned. This means keeping the cardiovascular system at a preinjury level and maintaining range of motion, strength, coordination, and muscle endurance of the uninjured limbs and joints. The whole body must be the focus of the rehabilitation program, not just the injured area. Remember that the total patient must be ready for return to normal activity or competition; providing the patient with a program to keep the uninvolved areas in peak condition, rather than just rehabilitating the injured area, will help you better prepare the patient physically and psychologically for when the injured area is completely rehabilitated.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-are-the-5-stages-of-rehabilitation">What are the 5 stages of rehabilitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-5-stages-of-rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stages of Rehabilitation</li>
<li>Phase 1 - Control Pain and Swelling.</li>
<li>Phase 2 - Improve Range of Motion and/or Flexibility.</li>
<li>Phase 3 - Improve Strength &amp; Begin Proprioception/Balance Training.</li>
<li>Phase 4 - Proprioception/Balance Training &amp; Sport-Specific Training.</li>
<li>Phase 5 - Gradual Return to Full Activity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-roles-in-rehab">Nursing Roles in Rehab<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-roles-in-rehab" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>☐ Caregiver</li>
<li>☐ Coordinator</li>
<li>☐ Educator</li>
<li>☐ Advocate</li>
<li>☐ Case Manager</li>
<li>☐ Leader</li>
<li>☐ Collaborator</li>
<li>☐ Facilitator</li>
<li>☐ Liaison</li>
<li>☐ Consultant</li>
<li>☐ Discharge planner</li>
<li>☐ Researcher</li>
<li>☐ Counselor</li>
<li>☐ Coach</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ad6901cf.jpeg" alt="img-190.jpeg"></p>
<p>Right to Treatment with dignity and respect</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Section 1 (a) of Article 54 requires that persons with disabilities be addressed and referred to in a manner that is not demeaning to them. This entitlement advocate for non-discrimination of persons with disabilities on any basis. Therefore, this Right requires all persons not to prejudice persons with disabilities because of their disability.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Access to educational institutions and facilities for PWDs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contained in Section 1(b), this entitlement requires that educational facilities be made comfortable for persons with disabilities. It advocates for the principles of accessibility, reasonable accommodation, and universal design in developing infrastructures such as buildings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Accessibility means that all structures are designed to allow a persons with disabilities to access them without any strain. It calls for buildings to have access ramps for wheelchairs, elevators, and handrails.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>3</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Reasonable access to all places, public transport, and information</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This entitlement in Section 1 (C) of Article 54 calls on the government to ensure that public infrastructures such as buildings and roads are friendly to persons with disabilities. Thus, it advocates for accessibility to facilitate movement with ease for persons with disabilities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also advocates for universal design to ensure that public facilities are easily accessible for PWDs without requiring no modification. The Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities (CRPD) defines universal design as “the design of products, environments, programs, and services to be usable by all people, to the greatest extent possible, without the need for adaptation or specialized design.”</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>4</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to the use of sign language, braille, or other appropriate means of communication</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This provision strives to ensure that PWDs who have visual or hearing impairments can communicate effectively. Article 7 of the Constitution complements this entitlement by calling for the promotion of sign language. It requires the government to "promote the development and use of indigenous languages, Kenyan Sign language, Braille and other communication formats and technologies accessible to persons with disabilities."</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sign language could become the country's third official language after English and Kiswahili if the National Assembly approves the Kenyan Sign Language Bill of 2021. The Bill, which the Senate has already approved, strives to ensure learners with hearing impairments are "taught in a manner in which they can understand and use the dominant language of instruction in the education system."</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should the Bill become law, all government institutions such as the judiciary, parastatals, and schools will be required to provide for the use of Sign Language.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>5</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to the accessibility of materials and devices to overcome constraints arising from the person's disability.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Article 54 (1) (e) of the Kenyan Constitution entitles persons with disabilities to the accessibility of assistive devices to become as independent as possible. Such assistive devices include crutches, wheelchairs, and hearing aids.</p>
</li>
</ul>
